Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Ten: In the view of both parties, the principle is that two testimonies are required: one to prove the ownership of the deceased, and the second to prove the ownership of the heir. But in the text's issue, one testimony is deemed sufficient, as it said: 'And he is not burdened with two testimonies' meaning the heir is not burdened with a second testimony. The answer is that the principle is that the heir would present two testimonies: one to prove the deceased's ownership, the second to prove his own ownership. However, in this issue, one testimony becomes sufficient. The need for two testimonies according to the principle is because the property inherited is a new and fresh ownership for the heir. Accordingly, a slave-girl inherited by the heir requires istibra' (waiting period to ensure she is not pregnant) upon the heir, just as istibra' is obligatory upon the buyer. And if the deceased (poor) had given something as charity, it becomes permissible for the wealthy heir. If the heir's ownership were not new and fresh, neither would istibra' be obligatory nor would the charity be permissible. So when the heir's ownership is new, it is necessary that it transferred from the deceased, i.e., a second testimony testifies that the deceased died and left this thing as inheritance. The result is that by the first testimony the deceased's ownership is proven, and by the second testimony the transfer from deceased to heir is proven. On this principle, besides the text's issue, many other issues are derived. And in the text's issue, reliance on one testimony is because when testimony is given at the time of death that the deceased's ownership existed, then at the time of death his ownership is proven. And when at the time of death the deceased's ownership is proven by testimony, then upon his death that ownership involuntarily transfers to the heir. So when ownership automatically transfers to the heir, there is no great need to present a testimony to prove it. And when there is no need to present a testimony, then only one testimony to prove the deceased's ownership suffices. Similarly, if at the time of death his possession of something is proven by testimony, then proving possession proves his ownership, and after the deceased's ownership is proven, upon his death that ownership automatically transfers to the heir. The result is that after proving the deceased's possession by testimony, there is no need to present testimony on his ownership, nor on its transfer to the heir. We will mention the full details on another occasion. In the text's issue, testimony on the deceased's possession is found as well: in the text's issue, the possession of the musta'ir (borrower), mudda' (trustee), and musta'jir (lessee) is proven by testimony, and the possession of these three persons stands in place of the deceased's possession. That is, proving the possession of the borrower, trustee, and lessee is in reality proving the deceased's possession. And when the deceased's possession is proven, his ownership is also proven. And when the ownership of the deceased (the claimant's father) is proven, then upon his death that ownership automatically transfers to the heir (the claimant). There will be no need for any testimony to prove the heir's ownership. And if they testify that it was in the hand of so-and-so and he died while it was in his hand, the testimony is admissible because at death the hand (possession) transforms into a hand of ownership by means of liability (daman), and the trust becomes guaranteed by leaving it unknown. So it becomes like testimony on the existence of his ownership at the time of death. Translation: If people testify that this house was in the possession of so-and-so and he died while the house was in his possession, then this testimony is admissible. Explanation: The scenario is that if witnesses testify that the house was in the possession of the claimant's (heir's) father until death and he died with the house in his possession, then the testimony is admissible and as a result the heir becomes the owner of the house. The deceased's (claimant's father's) possession has three forms: 1. That his possession was as an owner. 2. That his possession was as a usurper. 3. That his possession was as a trust. In the first case, undoubtedly the deceased's owned property transfers to his son's ownership because upon the deceased's death all his owned property transfers to his heirs. In the second case, since the deceased's possession was usurping, upon his death the usurped object becomes guaranteed upon him, and when daman becomes obligatory on the usurper, he becomes the owner of the usurped object. So when the usurper (the deceased) becomes the owner of the usurped object by the obligation of daman, then after his death the heir becomes its owner. In the third case, even if the deceased's possession was as a trust, but since he did not state whose trust it was and died leaving it unknown, then the deceased becomes the guarantor (damin) of it in the hereafter. And when he becomes the guarantor, he dies leaving it as his own property, and when the deceased dies leaving his own property, the heir becomes its owner. Therefore, at that time the deceased's possession, whether it was possession of ownership, possession of usurpation, or possession of trust, the heir becomes the owner of that thing. And there is no need for testimony that the deceased's ownership existed. But all this is on condition that the claimant's being an heir is established.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage discusses an exception in the law of evidence (shahada) concerning inheritance. The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that two separate testimonies are required for an heir to claim property: one to prove the deceased owned the property, and another to prove that ownership transferred to the heir upon death. However, the text (matn) states that in certain cases the heir is not burdened with producing a second testimony. The commentator explains the rationale: when testimony establishes the deceased's ownership at the moment of death, the transfer to the heir is automatic and involuntary, so it does not need separate proof. This is an application of istihsan, where the general rule is relaxed due to the nature of inheritance as a forced transfer. The passage then extends this logic to cases where the deceased's possession (qabda) is proven, regardless of whether that possession was as owner, usurper, or trustee. In each case, if the deceased died with the property in his hand, the possession is transformed into ownership upon death (for usurpers and trustees via daman liability). Therefore, one testimony proving possession at death suffices to establish the heir's ownership. The commentator also mentions that this ruling applies only when the claimant's status as heir is proven separately.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence/testimony; here specifically the testimony of witnesses (shuhud) to prove a claim.
مورث (muwarristh): The deceased person from whom property is inherited.
وارث (warith): The heir who inherits from the deceased.
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession; physical control over a property. The passage discusses how possession at death transforms into ownership by operation of law.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage. In this context, a usurper or trustee who does not identify the owner becomes liable, which transforms possession into ownership.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following statements accurately reflects the Hanafi rule on testimony in inheritance, as explained in this lesson?
A) One testimony always suffices in inheritance claims, regardless of circumstances.
B) One testimony suffices if it proves the deceased's possession at the time of death.
C) Two testimonies are always required, one for ownership and one for transfer.
D) One testimony suffices only if the deceased was the owner (not a usurper or trustee).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, proving the deceased's possession at death automatically establishes ownership and transfer to the heir, rendering a second testimony unnecessary — an application of istihsan.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Possession at Death: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Explains validity of testimony of possession at death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of possession at death, explain the rational proof (talil), and apply it to the three categories of possession.

Core Idea
At death, all possession—whether ownership, usurpation, or trust—transforms into ownership by guarantee.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya explains why the Hanafi school accepts testimony that a deceased person had possession of property at the time of death. At first glance, possession alone might not prove ownership, but the author provides a rational proof: at death, any unaccounted possession becomes guaranteed (ḍamān), thereby turning into presumptive ownership. The commentary elaborates on three possible types of possession, showing that each leads to the same outcome for inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being testified? The witnesses state that the deceased had possession of the property at the moment of death. The ruling is that such testimony is valid (jā'iz) and the heir inherits the property.
The act is giving testimony (shahāda) about a state at death.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof (dalīl) is a rational argument (talīl): 'the hands at death are turned into a hand of ownership by means of guarantee, and the trust becomes guaranteed by being left unknown.' This is found in the Arabic matn.
The proof is not a scriptural text but a reasoned principle based on legal consequences.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
How does this prove the ruling? The key phrase is 'by means of guarantee' (bi-wāsitat al-ḍamān). Possession at death, if it was not originally ownership, becomes guaranteed (ḍamān) either because the deceased was a usurper (liable to return) or because a trust was left unknown (making the trustee liable). Once guaranteed, the possessor becomes the owner for inheritance purposes, so the possession is equivalent to ownership.
This is a legal presumption (istiḥsān) based on the transformation of liability.
4
Analyze the three categories of possession
The commentary clarifies that possession at death falls into three types: ownership (milkiyya), usurpation (ghaṣb), and trust (amāna). In each case, at death it becomes ownership: ownership directly stays; usurpation becomes ownership because the usurper becomes liable; a trust becomes ownership because leaving it unknown makes the trustee liable.
This is essential for applying the rule: all three categories lead to the same result.
5
Note the ikhtilāf and tarjīḥ
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school (mukhtalaf fīh). Other schools may require explicit proof of ownership or may not accept the transformation argument. Within the Hanafi school, this is the established (muftā bihī) position from Ẓāhir al-Riwāya.
The proof is considered ẓannī al-thubūt (rational) but qaṭʿī al-dalāla (conclusive in meaning).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if they testify that it was in the hand of so-and-so, he died and it was in his hand[s], the testimony is permissible because the hands at death are turned into a hand of ownership by means of guarantee, and the trust becomes guaranteed by being left unknown, so it is like testimony on the establishment of his ownership at the time of death. Translation: And if people give testimony that this house was in the possession of so-and-so, he died while this house was present in his possession, then this testimony is permissible because the possession at death becomes ownership possession through guarantee, and the trust becomes guaranteed by leaving it unknown, so it becomes as if testimony on the existence of the claimant's father's ownership at the time of death. Explanation: The case is that if witnesses testify that the claimant's father had possession of this house until death and he died while the house was in his possession, then this testimony is valid and as a result the heir becomes the owner of this house. The possession of the predecessor has three types: 1- his possession was ownership, 2- his possession was usurpation, 3- his possession was trust. In the first case the owned property transfers to the heir without hesitation, because upon death all owned things transfer to the heirs. In the second case, due to guarantee, the usurped object becomes owned by the usurper at death, so it transfers to the heir. In the third case, even if it was trust, since he left it unknown, he becomes the guarantor at death and so it becomes his property, transferring to the heir. Therefore, whether possession is ownership, usurpation, or trust, the heir becomes owner. And there is no need for testimony that the predecessor's ownership was established. But all this is on condition that the claimant is known to be the heir.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on the validity of testimony that a deceased person had possession of property at the time of death. The author establishes that such testimony is admissible because possession at death necessarily transforms into presumptive ownership due to the principle of guarantee (ḍamān). The commentary then explains the three possible categories of possession: ownership, usurpation, and trust. In each case, at death the property becomes owned by the deceased (either originally or through guarantee) and thus transfers to the heir. This ruling is based on a rational proof (istihsān) derived from the fact that possession at death, when unspecified, is treated as ownership for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Possession or control over property; physical or legal custody.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee or liability; in this context, the responsibility to compensate for lost property, which can transform possession into ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because at death, any type of possession (ownership, usurpation, trust) becomes ownership through guarantee.
C) Because the heir's claim is stronger than the witness's testimony.
D) Because the deceased cannot dispute the testimony.

Key Takeaway
At death, all possession becomes presumptive ownership due to the mechanism of guarantee, so testimony of possession alone is sufficient for inheritance in the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Testimony of Past Possession
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony of past possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on testimony of past possession, state the arguments of Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Past possession is unknown; testimony about it is not accepted.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement: should testimony that a property was in the claimant's possession months ago be admissible when it is now in another's hands? The relied-upon position holds that such testimony is invalid because past possession can be ownership, trust, or guarantee – an unknown. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing possession to ownership. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes certainty in testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
What is the specific scenario and the legal question being debated?
The issue: testimony that a house was in claimant's possession months ago when defendant currently holds it.
2
State the Majority (Sahibayn) Position
What is the ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah? What is their core argument?
They say testimony not accepted because past possession is unknown in nature (majhul).
3
Present Imam Abu Yusuf's Position
How does Abu Yusuf argue for admissibility? What analogy does he use?
He analogizes possession to ownership and to testimony of taking (akhdh).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
How does the majority rebut Abu Yusuf? What distinguishes ownership from possession?
Ownership is uniform; possession is diverse. Also, news is not like witnessing.
5
Apply the Practical Consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? Who wins the case under each view?
Under majority: house stays with defendant. Under Abu Yusuf: returned to claimant.

And if they say to a living man, 'We testify that it was in the possession of the claimant for months,' it is not accepted. And from Ibn Yusuf [Abu Yusuf], it is accepted because possession is intended like ownership. If they testified that it was his ownership, it would be accepted, so likewise this. And it becomes as if they testified to taking from the claimant. The apparent view (which is the saying of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]) is that the testimony is based on an unknown because the possession is past and it is diverse: ownership, trust, and guarantee. Thus, judgment to return the unknown is difficult. Unlike ownership because it is known and not diverse. Unlike taking because it is known and its ruling is known—the obligation of return. And because the possession of the current possessor is witnessed, and the claimant's possession is testified to, and news is not like witnessing. Translation: And if witnesses said to a living person, 'This house was in the possession of so-and-so claimant for a few months,' then this testimony will not be accepted. And from Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that this testimony will be accepted because possession is intended like ownership. If witnesses testified that it was his ownership, it would be accepted, so likewise here. And it becomes as if witnesses testified to taking from the claimant. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the testimony is established over an unknown because the possession is past and it is of three types: ownership possession, trust possession, guarantee possession. So it is difficult to judge the return of the unknown. Unlike ownership, which is known and not diverse. Unlike taking, which is known and its ruling is known—the obligation of return. And because the possession of the current possessor is witnessed, and the claimant's possession is testified to, and news is not like witnessing. Explanation: The case is that there is a house in the possession of a living person, e.g., Khalid. Another person, e.g., Hamid, claims that this house is his, and the defendant (Khalid) denies it. Then the claimant (Hamid) brings evidence, and the witnesses say, 'We testify that the house was in the possession of the claimant (Hamid).' Then this testimony is not accepted, and consequently the house will not be returned to the claimant. This is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and also the Zahir al-Riwayah. And from Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the mentioned testimony is accepted and the house will be returned to the claimant. The phrase 'for a living person' is mentioned because if witnesses testify for a deceased that at the time of death the house was in his possession, then that testimony is accepted by consensus and the house will transfer to the heir. Anyway, in this disputed matter, Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that possession is intended like ownership, and the ruling on ownership is that if witnesses testify that this house which is currently in the possession of the defendant (Khalid) was the ownership of the claimant (Hamid), then that testimony is accepted. Similarly, when witnesses testify that this house was in the possession of the claimant (Hamid), then the testimony should be accepted and the house returned to the claimant. And it becomes like when witnesses testify that this house was in the possession of the claimant (Hamid) but the current possessor (the defendant) took it from the claimant (Hamid). In that case, testimony is accepted and the house is returned. So in this case, when witnesses testify that this house was in the possession of the claimant (Hamid)...
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of testimony that a property was in the claimant's possession months ago, when the property is currently in another's possession. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that such testimony is not accepted because past possession is of an unknown nature (ownership, trust, or guarantee), and the judge cannot rule based on an unknown. Imam Abu Yusuf analogizes possession to ownership, arguing that if testimony of ownership is accepted, so should testimony of possession. The majority (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) counter that ownership is a known state, while possession is multivalent. They also distinguish testimony of taking (which is specific and known) from general past possession. The difference has practical consequences: under Abu Yusuf's view, the house would be returned to the claimant; under the majority view, it would not.

Key Terms
يد منقضية (yad munqaḍiyah): Past or expired possession; possession that is no longer current.
شهادة على مجهول (shahāda ʿalā majhūl): Testimony about something unknown; here, the nature of the past possession is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, why is testimony that a house was in the claimant's possession months ago not accepted?
A) Because the claimant cannot prove ownership.
B) Because the past possession is of an unknown nature (ownership, trust, or guarantee).
C) Because the defendant's possession is stronger.
D) Because the witnesses are not reliable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not accept testimony of past possession of a living person because the nature of past possession is unknown and cannot serve as a reliable basis for a court ruling.

Testimony of Past Possession: Abu Yusuf vs. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting testimony of past possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwaya) rejects testimony of past possession and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-analogy, applying the distinction between known and unknown legal categories.

Core Idea
Possession is ambiguous; ownership is clear – testimony of past possession fails because the judge cannot restore an unknown type.

In property disputes, witnesses may testify that the claimant once held the property. But is that enough? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi debate: Abu Yusuf argues that possession is as important as ownership, but the school's relied-upon opinion (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) insists that past possession is legally ambiguous. Understanding this requires examining the categories of possession and the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi testimony law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the Hanafi majority position
The claimant seeks to reclaim a house currently in another's possession; witnesses say they saw the claimant in possession months ago. The Zahir al-Riwaya position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds this testimony invalid (la tuqbal).
The current possessor is alive; if deceased, testimony is accepted by consensus.
2
Locate Abu Yusuf's opposing position and his analogies
Abu Yusuf accepts the testimony, using two analogies: (1) possession is as sought-after as ownership, and testimony of past ownership is accepted; (2) testimony of a known taking (akhdh) from the claimant is accepted, so past possession should be analogous.
These analogies form the core of his dalil aqli.
3
Trace the Hanafi majority's rebuttal: possession is ambiguous
The majority responds that possession (yad) is not a single known category; it can be ownership (milk), trust (amanah), or guarantee (daman). Since the past possession is terminated and its type unknown, the judge cannot decree restoration of an unknown (majhul).
The key term 'majhul' (unknown) is central to the argument.
4
Contrast with ownership and taking
Unlike possession, ownership is a single, known legal category (ghayr mukhtalaf). Taking (akhdh) is a known act with a clear ruling (obligation to return). These differences break the analogies.
Ownership and taking are both 'ma'lum' (known), while past possession is 'majhul al-jins' (unknown type).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical difference: under the majority, the house stays with the current possessor; under Abu Yusuf, it is returned. The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwaya position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), because testimony on an unknown cannot be adjudicated.
The text explicitly states 'وجه الظاهر وهو قولهما' (the manifest position is their statement).

قبضہ زائل ہو چکا ہے حالانکہ قبضہ تین طرح کا ہوتا ہے ۔ قبضہ ملک،قبضہ امانت ،قبضہ ضمان ۔ پس مجہول قبضہ کے اعادہ کا حکم دینا متعذر ہے برخلاف ملک کے اس لئے کہ وہ معلوم اور غیر مختلف ہے اور بر خلاف لے لینے اور گواہوں نے یہ کہا کہ ہم گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ مکان مدعی یعنی حامد کے قبضہ میں تھا تو یہ گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور اس گواہی کے نتیجہ میں یہ مکان مدعی کو واپس نہیں کرایا جائے گا۔ طرفین کا قول بھی یہی ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ بھی یہی ہے اور حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ مذکورہ گواہی قبول کر کے مکان مدعی کی طرف واپس کرایا جائے گا۔ متر میں جل کے حسی کی قید اس لئے ذکر کی گئی ہے کہ اگر گواہ میت کے لئے یہ گواہی دیں کہ موت کے وقت کے مکان اس میت کے قبضہ میں تھا تو یہ گواہی بالا جماع قبول ہوگی اور یہ مکان وارث کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا۔ بہر حال مختلف فیہ مسئلہ میں امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قبضہ اسطرح مقصود ہوتا ہے جس طرح ملک مقصود ہوتی ہے اور ملک کے بارے میں حکم یہ ہے کہ گواہ اگر یہ گواہی دیں کہ یہ مکان جو اس وقت مدعی علیہ یعنی خالد کے قبضہ میں ہے مدعی یعنی حامد کی ملک تھا تو یہ گواہی قبول ہوتی ہے اسی طرح جب گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ یہ مکان مدعی یعنی حامد کے قبضہ میں تھا تو بھی گواہی قبول ہوگی اور مکان مدعی کو واپس کرایا جائیگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ جیسے گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ یہ مکان تو مدعی یعنی حامد کے قبضہ میں تھا لیکن مدعی علیہ جو اس وقت قابض ہے اس نے مدعی یعنی حامد سے لے لیا تھا تو اس صورت میں گواہی قبول کر لی جاتی ہے اور مکان مدعی کو واپس کر دیا جاتا ہے پس اس طرح جب گواہ یہ گواہی دیں کہ یہ مکان مدعی یعنی حامد کے قبضہ میں تھا تو اس گواہی کو بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور مکان مدعی کو واپس کرا دیا جائے گا۔ ظاہر الروایہ یعنی طرفین کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فی الحال مدعی ( حامد ) کا قبضہ موجود نہیں ہے اور ماضی میں جس قبضہ کی گواہوں نے گواہی دی ہے وہ تین طرح کا ہو سکتا۔ ا ہے ا مالکانہ قبضہ ۔ یعنی یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں اس لئے ہو کہ مدعی اس کا مالک تھا۔ ۲ امانت کا قبضہ یعنی یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں ودیعت اور امانت کے طور پر تھا۔ ۔ نعمان کا قبضہ۔ یعنی یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں بطور غصب کے تھا یعنی مدعی نے غصب کرکے اس مکان پر قبضہ کر لیا تھا۔ بہر حال جب ایسا ہے تو مدعی کا قبضہ مجہول ہوا اور شہادت مجبول قبضہ پر قائم ہوئی حالانکہ مجہول چیز کے بارے میں قاضی کا حکم کرنا متعذر ہے، پس جب مجہول چیز کے بارے میں قضائے قاضی متعذر ہے تو قیام جہالت کے ساتھ اس قبضہ کے اعادہ کا حکم کرنا بھی متعذر ہوگا۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ ( قابض ) کا قبضہ ختم کرا کر مدعی کو دوبارہ قبضہ نہیں دلایا جائے گا۔ بخلاف الملک الخ سے امام یوسف کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ اس مکان کا مالک مدعی ( حامد ) ہے تو اس گواہی کو اس لئے قبول کر لیا جائے گا کہ ملک معلوم ہے غیر مختلف ہے یعنی ملک فقط ایک ہی طرح کی ہوتی ہے اگر چہ اس کے اسباب مختلف ہوتے ہیں پس جب ملک معلوم اور غیر مختلف ہے تو گواہی معلوم چیز پر قائم ہوئی اور جب گواہی معلوم چیز پر قائم ہوئی تو قاضی کا فیصلہ کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اور جب قاضی کا فیصلہ کرناممکن ہے تو قاضی مذکورہ گواہی کے نتیجہ میں یہ حکم کرے گا کہ یہ مکان مدعی ( مامد ) کا ہے لہذا اس کو مدعی کی طرف واپس کیا جائے۔ و بخلاف الاخذ الخ سے دوسرے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ مدعی علیہ ( قابض) نے یہ مکان مدعی سے لے لیا تھا یعنی نصب کر لیا تھا تو شہادت کے ذریعہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مدعی علیہ کا یہ قبضہ غاصبانہ ہے اور اس کا حکم بھی معلوم ہے یعنی مدعی (مغصوب منہ) کی طرف اس کا واپس کرنا واجب ہے، لہذا اس صورت میں بھی قاضی اس مکان کو مدعی کی طرف واپس کرنے کا حکم کرے گا۔ طرفین کی طرف سے دوسری دلیل یہ ہیکہ قابض یعنی مدعی علیہ کا قبضہ آنکھوں سے مشاہد ہے اور مدعی کے قبضہ کی فقط شہادت دی گئی ہے، اور شہادت ایک خبر ہے اور خبر مشاہدہ کے برابر ہرگز نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ مشاہدہ مفید یقین ہوتا ہے اور خبر مفید ظن ہوتی ہے. پس مشاہدہ کے ذریعہ جو قبضہ ثابت ہے وہ رائج ہوگا اور خبر یعنی شہادت کے ذریعہ جو قبضہ ثابت ہوا ہے وہ مرجوح ہوگا . اور تربیح راج کو حاصل ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مرجوح کو، لہذا بدعی علیہ یعنی قابض کے قبضہ کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی اور مکان اسی کے قبضے میں رہے گا، مدعی کی طرف واپس نہیں کرایا جائے گا۔
If they say to a living man, 'We testify that this was in the possession of the claimant for months,' it is not accepted. And from Ibn Yusuf [Abu Yusuf] it is narrated that it is accepted because possession is sought-after like ownership. If they testified that it was his property, it is accepted, so likewise this. And it becomes as if they testified about taking from the claimant. The manifest position (Zahir al-Riwaya) is the statement of the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] that the testimony is based on an unknown (majhul) because the possession is terminated and it is diverse into ownership, trust, and guarantee. So judgment is impossible due to restoring the unknown, unlike ownership because it is known and not varying, and unlike taking because it is known and its ruling is known—which is the obligation of return. And because the hand of the current possessor is observed, and the hand of the claimant is testified to, and a report is not like observation. [Urdu translation and commentary: Explanation of the case and arguments]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding testimony of past possession. The issue: witnesses testify that a house was in the claimant's possession for several months, but the current possessor is a living man. The Zahir al-Riwaya position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that such testimony is not accepted. Their reasoning: possession (yad) is a general term that can be ownership, trust, or guarantee (e.g., usurped). Since the past possession is no longer present and its type is unknown (majhul), a judge cannot pass a decree to restore it. This differs from testimony of ownership (which is a single known concept) or testimony of a known taking (which has a clear ruling of return). Additionally, the current possessor's possession is directly observed (mushahad), providing certainty, whereas the claimant's past possession is only reported (khabar), which gives only probability (zann). The observed possession prevails. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, analogizes from ownership: since possession is as important as ownership, and testimony of past ownership is accepted, so too should testimony of past possession be accepted. He also analogizes from testimony of a known taking. The reply from the two shaykhs distinguishes ownership and known taking as unambiguous, whereas past possession is ambiguous. The text then provides detailed Urdu commentary, including the condition that the possessor must be alive; if the possessor is deceased, testimony of past possession is accepted by consensus because the property passes to heirs. The final ruling in fatwa is the Zahir al-Riwaya position: testimony of past possession from a living man is not accepted.

Key Terms
ید (yad): Possession/hand; a legal concept of control over property, which can be based on ownership, trust, or guarantee.
قبضہ (qabda): Possession; synonymous with yad in this context, used in Urdu commentary.
مشاہد (mushahad): Directly observed; evidence based on eyewitness certainty.
مجهول (majhul): Unknown; a fact or object that is indeterminate in type or quantity.
قبضہ ملک (qabda milk): Possession based on ownership.
قبضہ امانت (qabda amanat): Possession as a trust (e.g., deposit).
قبضہ ضمان (qabda daman): Possession under guarantee or usurpation (ghasb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwaya position, why is testimony that a house was in the claimant's possession not accepted when the current possessor is alive?
A) Because testimony from witnesses is generally not accepted in property cases.
B) Because past possession is unknown in type (ownership, trust, or guarantee), making judgment impossible.
C) Because the claimant must prove ownership, not just possession.
D) Because the current possessor has a stronger right to the property.

Key Takeaway
Testimony of past possession is not accepted because possession is legally ambiguous; only testimony of ownership or a known taking suffices to adjudicate.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Admission and Testimony of Admission: Possession Returned Upon Acknowledgment
Ruling on effect of admission and testimony thereof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that ignorance of the thing admitted does not invalidate an admission and apply it to distinguish between testimony of past possession and testimony of admission.

Core Idea
An admission is valid even if the thing admitted is unknown; testimony about the admission itself is acceptable because the admission is known.

In legal claims, the nature of past possession can be ambiguous. However, the Hanafi school rules that when a defendant admits that the property was once in the claimant's hand, that admission alone suffices to order return. Why? Because the law gives weight to admissions against one's own interest. And if witnesses testify to that admission, the testimony is also accepted — not because the possession is known, but because the admission itself is a known act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two ways property can be returned: (1) defendant admits past possession, (2) two witnesses testify that defendant made such an admission. Recognize that both lead to the same outcome but through different reasoning.
Focus on the legal basis for each.
2
Apply the principle of iqrar
For the first scenario, the rule 'jahala fi al-muqarr bih la tamna' sihhat al-iqrar' (ignorance of the thing admitted does not prevent validity of admission) is cited. Understand that this principle allows vague admissions to be effective.
This is a key Hanafi maxim distinguishing iqrar from shahada.
3
Distinguish the basis for testimony
For the second scenario, note that the subject of testimony (mashhud bih) is the admission itself, which is a known and definite act. The ambiguity of the past possession is irrelevant because the testimony is about the admission, not the possession.
Compare with direct testimony of past possession (previous lesson) where possession type is unknown.
4
Contrast with direct testimony of past possession
If witnesses directly testify that the property was in claimant's possession without an admission, the property is not returned because the nature of possession is unknown. This contrast highlights why the admission changes the ruling.
The admission removes ambiguity by being a clear declaration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اقر بذلك المدعى عليه دفعت الى المدعى لان الجهالة فى المقربه لا تمنع صحة الاقرار وان شهد شاهدان انه اقرانها كانت فى يد المدعى دفعت اليه لان المشهود به ههنا الاقرار وهو معلوم . ترجمہ اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے اس کا اقرار کیا تو یہ مکان مدعی کو واپس دلایا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ مقر بہ کا مجہول ہونا اقرار کی صحت کو مانع نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر دو گواہ گواہی دیں کہ مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا تھا کہ یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضے میں تھا تو مکان مدعی کو واپس دلایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہاں مشہود بہ اقرار ہے جو معلوم ہے۔
If the defendant admits that, it is given to the claimant, because ignorance (jahala) of the thing admitted (muqarr bih) does not prevent the validity of admission. And if two witnesses testify that he admitted that it was in the hand of the claimant, it is given to him, because the testified thing (mashhud bih) here is the admission, which is known. [Urdu translation: And if the defendant admits this, the house will be returned to the claimant, because the thing admitted being unknown does not prevent the validity of the admission. And if two witnesses testify that the defendant admitted that the house was in the claimant's possession, the house will be returned to the claimant, because the testified thing here is the admission, which is known.]
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage states two related rulings. First, if the defendant (current possessor) admits that the property was previously in the claimant's possession, then the property is returned to the claimant. This is because in an admission (iqrar), ignorance (jahala) of the thing admitted does not invalidate the admission. The mere fact of admission creates a right. Second, if witnesses testify that the defendant made such an admission, then the property is also returned to the claimant. This is because the subject of the testimony is the admission itself, which is a known act, not the ambiguous nature of the past possession. The admission is a clear declaration that is known, so the testimony is valid. This contrasts with the previous case where witnesses directly testified about past possession without admission; there, the possession's nature was unknown. Here, the admission provides a clear basis for the judge to order return. The Urdu commentary adds that the admission is acceptable even if the thing admitted is unknown in detail, because iqrar is a form of declaration against oneself, and the law accepts it liberally.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Admission/confession by a party in a legal claim; a declaration against one's own interest.
مقربه (muqarr bih): The thing admitted; the subject of the iqrar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the defendant admits that the house was in the claimant's possession, why does the judge return the house despite not knowing what type of possession it was?
A) Because the judge has a general power to decide.
B) Because the admission is against the defendant's own interest, so it is trustworthy by default.
C) Because ignorance of the thing admitted does not prevent the validity of admission.
D) Because the claimant's witnesses were stronger.

Key Takeaway
Admission (iqrar) is valid even if the thing admitted is unknown, and testimony about an admission is accepted because the admission itself is a known act.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Why Testimony of Past Possession Without Specification Is Not Accepted
Explains why testimony of past possession without specification is not accepted in Hanafi law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of past possession and explain why it is not accepted based on ambiguity and the epistemological weight of direct observation.

Core Idea
Ambiguous past possession cannot override directly witnessed present possession.

In property disputes, testimony about a party's past possession often arises. The Hanafi school distinguishes between testimony that merely states past possession and testimony that clarifies the legal nature of that possession. This lesson examines the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah and its rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Determine the ruling on testimony of past possession without specifying its legal type. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, such testimony is not accepted, and the defendant retains the property.
The ruling is attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the three possible types of past possession
Past possession can be of three types: ownership (milk), trust (amanah), or usurpation (ghasb). Since the witnesses did not specify which type, the possession is ambiguous (majhul).
The judge cannot rule on an ambiguous matter.
3
Understand the epistemological proof
The defendant's current possession is directly witnessed (mushahada), which yields certainty (yaqin). Testimony (shahada) is a report that yields only conjecture (zann). Certainty prevails over conjecture, so the defendant's possession remains.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
4
Distinguish the exceptions
Testimony that explicitly states ownership or that the defendant took the property (usurped) is accepted because these are known and unambiguous. Ownership is singular and non-variable; usurpation is a known act with a known ruling (return).
These exceptions confirm the general rule through contrast.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a scenario with witnesses testifying only to past possession, decide that the testimony is insufficient and the defendant retains possession. If additional details clarify the type, reconsider.
Practice tasks will reinforce application.

Source Text

تھا تو اس گواہی کو بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور مکان مدعی کو واپس کرا دیا جائے گا۔ ظاہر الروایہ یعنی طرفین کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فی الحال مدعی ( حامد ) کا قبضہ موجود نہیں ہے اور ماضی میں جس قبضہ کی گواہوں نے گواہی دی ہے وہ تین طرح کا ہو سکتا ہے: ا مالکانہ قبضہ ۔ یعنی یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں اس لئے ہو کہ مدعی اس کا مالک تھا۔ ۲ امانت کا قبضہ یعنی یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں ودیعت اور امانت کے طور پر تھا۔ ۳ غصب کا قبضہ۔ یعنی یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں بطور غصب کے تھا یعنی مدعی نے غصب کرکے اس مکان پر قبضہ کر لیا تھا۔ بہر حال جب ایسا ہے تو مدعی کا قبضہ مجہول ہوا اور شہادت مجہول قبضہ پر قائم ہوئی حالانکہ مجہول چیز کے بارے میں قاضی کا حکم کرنا مستعد رہے، پس جب مجہول چیز کے بارے میں قضائے قاضی مستعد ہے تو قیام جہالت کے ساتھ اس قبضہ کے اعادہ کا حکم کرنا بھی متعد رہو گا۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ ( قابض ) کا قبضہ ختم کرا کر مدعی کو دوبارہ قبضہ نہیں دلایا جائے گا۔ بخلاف الملک الخ سے امام یوسف کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ اس مکان کا مالک مدعی ( حامد ) ہے تو اس گواہی کو اس لئے قبول کر لیا جائے گا کہ ملک معلوم ہے غیر مختلف ہے یعنی ملک فقط ایک ہی طرح کی ہوتی ہے اگر چہ اس کے اسباب مختلف ہوتے ہیں پس جب ملک معلوم اور غیر مختلف ہے تو گواہی معلوم چیز پر قائم ہوئی اور جب گواہی معلوم چیز پر قائم ہوئی تو قاضی کا فیصلہ کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اور جب قاضی کا فیصلہ کرناممکن ہے تو قاضی مذکورہ گواہی کے نتیجہ میں یہ حکم کرے گا کہ یہ مکان مدعی ( مامد ) کا ہے لہذا اس کو مدعی کی طرف واپس کیا جائے۔ و بخلاف الاخذ الخ سے دوسرے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ مدعی علیہ ( قابض) نے یہ مکان مدعی سے لے لیا تھا یعنی نصب کر لیا تھا تو شہادت کے ذریعہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مدعی علیہ کا یہ قبضہ غاصبانہ ہے اور اس کا حکم بھی معلوم ہے یعنی مدعی (مغصوب منہ) کی طرف اس کا واپس کرنا واجب ہے، لہذا اس صورت میں بھی قاضی اس مکان کو مدعی کی طرف واپس کرنے کا حکم کرے گا۔ طرفین کی طرف سے دوسری دلیل یہ ہیکہ قابض یعنی مدعی علیہ کا قبضہ آنکھوں سے مشاہد ہے اور مدعی کے قبضہ کی فقط شہادت دی گئی ہے، اور شہادت ایک خبر ہے اور خبر مشاہدہ کے برابر ہرگز نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ مشاہدہ مفید یقین ہوتا ہے اور خبر مفید ظن ہوتی ہے. پس مشاہدہ کے ذریعہ جو قبضہ ثابت ہے وہ رائج ہوگا اور خبر یعنی شہادت کے ذریعہ جو قبضہ ثابت ہوا ہے وہ مرجوح ہوگا . اور ترجیح راج کو حاصل ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مرجوح کو، لہذا بدعی علیہ یعنی قابض کے قبضہ کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی اور مکان اسی کے قبضے میں رہے گا، مدعی کی طرف واپس نہیں کرایا جائے گا۔
Then this testimony will also be accepted and the house will be returned to the plaintiff. The reason according to Zahir al-Riwayah, i.e., the saying of the two parties (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), is that currently the plaintiff's possession does not exist, and the past possession which the witnesses testified about can be of three types: (1) Possession of ownership – i.e., the house was in the plaintiff's possession because he was its owner. (2) Possession of trust – i.e., it is possible that the house was in the plaintiff's possession as a deposit or trust. (3) Possession of usurpation – i.e., the house was in the plaintiff's possession by way of usurpation, meaning the plaintiff had usurped it and taken possession. In any case, since this is so, the plaintiff's possession is ambiguous and the testimony is based on ambiguous possession, while it is not permissible for a judge to pass judgment on an ambiguous thing. Therefore, when it is not permissible for a judge to pass judgment on an ambiguous thing, then ruling for the re-establishment of that possession along with the ambiguity is also not permissible. That is, the possession of the defendant will not be terminated and the plaintiff will not be re-possessed. This is the answer to the analogy of Imam Yusuf from 'bikhilaf al-milk'. The summary of the answer is that if the witnesses testify that the plaintiff is the owner of this house, then this testimony will be accepted because ownership is known and not variable – i.e., ownership is only of one type even though its causes vary. So when ownership is known and non-variable, the testimony is based on a known thing, and when the testimony is based on a known thing, it is possible for the judge to decide. And when it is possible for the judge to decide, the judge will rule based on that testimony that this house belongs to the plaintiff, therefore it will be returned to him. This is the answer to the second analogy from 'bikhilaf al-akhdh'. The summary is that when the witnesses testify that the defendant had taken this house from the plaintiff, i.e., usurped it, then through the testimony it becomes known that the defendant's possession is usurpation and its ruling is also known – i.e., it is obligatory to return it to the plaintiff (the one from whom it was usurped). Therefore in this case too, the judge will order the return of the house to the plaintiff. The second proof from the two parties is that the possession of the defendant is directly witnessed, while only testimony has been given about the plaintiff's possession. Testimony is a report, and a report can never be equal to direct observation, because direct observation yields certainty while a report yields conjecture. So the possession proven through direct observation will prevail, and the possession proven through testimony will be preponderated. And precedence is given to the preponderant, not the preponderated. Therefore the possession of the defendant will have precedence and the house will remain in his possession; it will not be returned to the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Ashraf al-Hidaya. It addresses a scenario where witnesses testify that the plaintiff had possession of a property in the past, but the property is currently in the defendant's possession. According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), such testimony is not accepted because past possession can be of three types: ownership, trust, or usurpation. Since the type is ambiguous, the judge cannot base a ruling on it. The text then contrasts two cases: (1) if witnesses testify to ownership directly, the testimony is accepted because ownership is a singular known status; (2) if witnesses testify that the defendant took the property (usurped), it is also accepted because the taking is a known act. The passage also gives a second rational proof: the defendant's current possession is witnessed directly (mushahada), which yields certainty, while the testimony about past possession is only a report (khabar), which yields conjecture. Certainty prevails over conjecture, so the defendant retains possession.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession of a property, which can be of three types: ownership, trust, or usurpation.
ملک (milk): Ownership, a singular and non-variable legal status.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony given by witnesses in court, considered a report (khabar) and thus yields conjecture (zann), not certainty (yaqin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is testimony about the plaintiff's past possession not accepted when the defendant currently holds the property?
A) Because the plaintiff cannot prove ownership
B) Because past possession can be of multiple types (ownership, trust, usurpation) and is therefore ambiguous
C) Because the defendant's possession is witnessed directly and always prevails
D) Because testimony is not allowed in property disputes

Key Takeaway
Testimony of past possession without specifying its type is not accepted in Hanafi law due to ambiguity; the defendant's currently witnessed possession prevails.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Confession of Past Possession and Its Effect
Ruling on confession of past possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a defendant's confession of past possession and explain why ambiguity in the thing confessed does not affect validity.

Core Idea
A confession stands even if the thing confessed is vague; ambiguity does not bar validity.

In previous lessons, we learned that testimony of past possession alone is insufficient. But here, a defendant's confession that the property was in the plaintiff's possession carries weight. The key is a fundamental Hanafi principle: ambiguity (jahalah) in the thing confessed (muqarr bihi) does not invalidate the confession. This lesson unpacks that rule and its application when the confession is proven by witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core act and its ruling
Locate the act being ruled upon: the defendant's confession that the property was in the plaintiff's possession. The ruling is that the property is returned to the plaintiff based on this confession.
Focus on the confession itself, not the underlying ownership.
2
Recognize the principle governing ambiguity
The passage states that 'ambiguity in the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession.' Identify that the 'thing confessed' (muqarr bihi) is the past possession, the type of which may be unknown.
This principle is unique to Hanafi fiqh and distinguishes iqrar from testimony.
3
Extend the ruling to testimony of the confession
Notice that the same outcome applies if two witnesses testify that the defendant made such a confession. The testimonial focus is the confession (a known act), not the ambiguous possession.
This reinforces the principle: the validity hinges on the known act of confessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اقر بذلك المدعى عليه دفعت الى المدعى لان الجهالة فى المقربه لا تمنع صحة الاقرار وان شهد شاهدان انه اقر انها كانت فى يد المدعى دفعت اليه لان المشهود به ههنا الاقرار وهو معلوم . ترجمہ اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے اس کا اقرار کیا تو یہ مکان مدعی کو واپس دلایا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ مقر بہ کا مجہول ہونا اقرار کی صحت کو مانع نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر دو گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ مدعی علیہ نے یہ اقرار کیا ہے کہ یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں تھا تو یہ مکان مدعی کو واپس دلایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس جگہ مشہود بہ اقرار ہے اور وہ معلوم ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مدعی علیہ ( قابض ) نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں تھا تو یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں واپس دیا جائے گا، کیونکہ جس چیز کا اقرار کیا ہے اگر وہ مجہول ہو یعنی یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ کس قسم کا قبضہ مدعی کو حاصل تھا تو بھی یہ اقرار صحیح ہے اور مقر بہ کی جہالت صحت اقرار کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے لہذا مدعی علیہ کے اقرار کے موافق وہ مکان مدعی کو واپس دیا جائے گا اگر چہ اس سے مدعی کی ملکیت ثابت نہ ہو گی۔ اسی طرح اگر دو گواہوں نے یوں گواہی دی کہ مدعی علیہ نے یہ اقرار کیا ہے کہ یہ مکان اس مدعی کے قبضہ میں ہو تو بھی مدعی کو واپس دلا دیا جائے گا کیونکہ گواہوں نے جس چیز کی گواہی دی ہے وہ اقرار ہے اور اقرار ایک معلوم چیز ہے اگر چہ مقر بہ یعنی نوعیت قبضہ مجہول ہے۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ مقر بہ کی جہالت مانع نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی گواہی کے موافق وہ مکان مدعی کو واپس دلایا جائے گا اگر چہ اس سے مدعی کی ملکیت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔
And if the defendant confesses to that, it is handed over to the plaintiff because ambiguity in the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. And if two witnesses testify that he confessed that it was in the plaintiff's possession, it is handed over to the plaintiff because the thing testified about here is the confession, and it is known. Translation: If the defendant confesses, this house will be returned to the plaintiff. Because ambiguity of the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. And if two witnesses testify that the defendant confessed that this house was in the plaintiff's possession, then this house will be returned to the plaintiff because here the testified thing is the confession and it is known. Explanation: If the defendant confesses that this house was in the plaintiff's possession, then this house will be returned to the plaintiff's possession, because even if the thing confessed is ambiguous – i.e., it is not known what type of possession the plaintiff had – still this confession is valid, and ambiguity in the thing confessed is not a hindrance to the validity of the confession. Therefore, in accordance with the defendant's confession, that house will be returned to the plaintiff, even though ownership is not proven for the plaintiff. Similarly, if two witnesses testify that the defendant confessed that this house was in the plaintiff's possession, then also the house will be returned to the plaintiff, because what the witnesses testified about is the confession, and the confession is a known thing even though the thing confessed (the type of possession) is ambiguous. And it has passed earlier that ambiguity in the thing confessed is not a prevention. Therefore in this case too, according to the testimony, the house will be returned to the plaintiff, even though ownership is not proven for the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling contrasting with the previous lesson. While testimony of past possession alone is insufficient, a confession by the defendant that the property was in the plaintiff's possession is accepted. The key principle is that ambiguity (jahalah) in the thing confessed (muqarr bihi) does not invalidate the confession. The confession itself is a known act, and its validity does not require knowledge of the specific type of possession. The same applies if witnesses testify to the confession—the testimony is about the confession, which is known, not about the ambiguous possession. In both cases, the property is returned to the plaintiff, but this does not establish ownership; it only re-establishes possession.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission. In this context, it is accepted even if the thing confessed is ambiguous.
مقر بہ (muqarr bihi): The thing confessed. Here, it is the past possession of the plaintiff, the type of which may be unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the defendant confesses that the property was in the plaintiff's possession, what does the confession establish?
A) It establishes ownership of the plaintiff.
B) It establishes that the plaintiff had possession at some point, and the property is returned.
C) It is only valid if the confession is made in court.
D) It establishes that the plaintiff's possession was lawful.

Key Takeaway
A defendant's confession of past possession is accepted even if the type of possession is unknown, and the property is returned to the plaintiff without establishing ownership.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner

Testimony upon Testimony: Permissibility, Scope, and Istihsan Reasoning
Defines secondary testimony and states its permissibility with istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony upon testimony and identify its scope based on istihsan reasoning.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is permissible in all rights not repelled by doubt, based on istihsan to prevent loss of rights.

This lesson introduces the concept of secondary testimony (shahada ala al-shahada) as defined in Ashraf al-Hidaya. The Hanafi school permits it in financial and other non-hudud rights, relying on istihsan due to the pressing need to avoid loss of rights. However, because it involves a substitution and increased chance of error, it is not accepted in hudud and qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept and its form
The passage defines shahada ala al-shahada: original witnesses who cannot attend court appoint a deputy to testify on their behalf. Recognize that this is a secondary testimony derived from the original.
The deputy is not an eyewitness; he transmits the original witness's account.
2
State the ruling
The passage states that testimony upon testimony is permissible (ja'iz) in every right that is not defeated by doubt. Identify the hukm level: jawaz (permissible).
The ruling is qualified: it applies only to rights that survive doubt.
3
Understand the evidence: istihsan
The ruling is based on istihsan, not strict analogy. The text says 'this is istihsan due to severe need'. Grasp that the need to preserve rights overrides the literal prohibition that might arise from qiyas.
Istihsan is a Hanafi tool allowing departure from analogy for a stronger reason.
4
Recognize the limit: shubha excludes hudud and qisas
Secondary testimony involves a doubt (shubha) due to substitution and increased probability of error. Matters that are repelled by doubt, such as hudud and qisas, do not accept this form of testimony.
The principle: 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are repelled by doubts).
5
Note the practical effect
The ruling balances preserving rights (in financial matters, etc.) and protecting severe punishments from any taint of doubt. Identify which rights are included and which are excluded.
Included: debts, property, marriage contracts. Excluded: hadd penalties, qisas.

باب الشهادة على الشهادة جمیل احمد عفی عنہ ترجمہ یہ باب گواہی پر گواہی دینے کے بیان میں ہے تشریح شہادت علی الشہادت چونکہ شہادت اصول کی فرع ہے اس لئے شہادت علی الشہادت کو مؤخر کیا گیا۔ کیونکہ اصل ، فرع پر مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ شہادت علی الشہادت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ اصل گواہ جنہوں نے معاملہ کا مشاہد کیا ہے یا براہ راست سُنا ہے شہادت میں اپنا نائب بنا کر مجلس قاضی میں بھیج دیں۔ شہادت علی الشہادت کون سے حق پر دینا جائز ہے قال الشهادة على الشهادة جائزة فى كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة وهذا استحسان لشدة الحاجة اليها اذ شاهد الاصل قد يعجز عن اداء الشهادة لبعض العوارض فلو لم يجز الشهادة على الشهادة ادى الى اتواء الحقوق ولهذا جوزنا الشهادة على الشهادة وان كثرت الا ان فيها شبهة من حيث البدلية او من حيث ان فيها زيادة احتمال وقد امكن الاحتراز عنه بجنس الشهود فلا تقبل فيما يندرىء بالشبهات كالحدود والقصاص ترجمه گواہی پر گواہی دینا ہر ایسے حق میں جائز ہے جو شبہ سے ساقط نہ ہوتا ہو ، اور یہ استحسان ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی ضرورت زیادہ ہے اس لئے کہ اصل گواہ کبھی بعض عوارض کی وجہ سے عاجز ہوتا ہے پس اگر شہادت علی الشہادت جائز نہ ہو تو حقوق کو رائیگاں کر دینے کا سبب ہوگا۔ اسی وجہ سے ہم نے شہادت علی الشہادت کو جائز کر دیا ، اگر چہ شہود فرع کثیر ہوں لیکن اس میں شبہ ہے بدلیت کے اعتبار سے یا اس اعتبار سے کہ اس میں زیادہ احتمال ہے حالانکہ جنس شہود کے ذریعہ اس سے احتراز ممکن ہے۔ لہذا ایسی چیزوں میں قبول نہ ہو گی جو شبہات سے دور ہو جاتی ہیں۔ جیسے حدود اور قصاص ۔
Chapter: Testimony upon Testimony. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah pardon him. Translation: This chapter is about giving testimony upon testimony. Explanation: Testimony upon testimony, since it is a branch of original testimony, it is delayed because the original precedes the branch. The form of testimony upon testimony is that the original witnesses who witnessed the matter or directly heard it, appoint a deputy and send him to the judge's court. On which right is testimony upon testimony permissible? He said: Testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not defeated by doubt, and this is istihsan due to the severe need for it, because the original witness may be unable to perform testimony due to some impediments. So if testimony upon testimony were not permissible, it would lead to the loss of rights. For this reason we have permitted testimony upon testimony even if the subordinate witnesses are many. However, there is a doubt in it either because of substitution or because there is an increased possibility (of error), while it is possible to avoid that by the type of witnesses. Therefore it is not accepted in matters that are repelled by doubts, such as hudud and qisas. Translation: Giving testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not nullified by doubt, and this is istihsan. Because the need for it is great, as the original witness may be unable to perform testimony due to some impediments. So if testimony upon testimony were not permissible, it would cause rights to be wasted. For this reason we have permitted testimony upon testimony, even if the subordinate witnesses are many. But there is a doubt in it either in terms of substitution or because there is an increased probability (of error), while it is possible to avoid that by the type of witnesses. Therefore it is not accepted in matters that are repelled by doubts, such as hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada) from Ashraf al-Hidaya. It first defines the concept: original witnesses who are unable to attend court due to an impediment can appoint a deputy to testify on their behalf. The ruling is that this form of testimony is permissible in every right that is not defeated by doubt (shubha), based on istihsan due to the pressing need to preserve rights. If the original witness is absent or incapacitated, disallowing secondary testimony would lead to loss of rights. However, because secondary testimony involves a substitution (badaliyya) and an increased risk of error (ziyada ihtimal), it is not accepted in cases where even a slight doubt repels the punishment, such as hudud and qisas. The text emphasizes that despite the doubt, the necessity justifies its acceptance in financial and other non-hudud matters.

Key Terms
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony given by a deputy witness who was not present at the original event, based on the original witness's account.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that allows departing from strict analogy for a stronger reason, here the need to preserve rights.
شبهہ (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents application of severe punishments. In this context, the shubha arises from the substitution and increased probability of error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony upon testimony not accepted in hudud and qisas according to this passage?
A) Because the original witness must be present
B) Because there is a doubt (shubha) in secondary testimony due to substitution and increased possibility of error
C) Because hudud and qisas require multiple witnesses
D) Because the defendant has the right to cross-examine

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is valid in rights unaffected by doubt; istihsan preserves rights, but shubha excludes hudud and qisas.

Testimony upon Testimony: Ruling and Istihsan Basis
Defines shahada ala al-shahada and its ruling via istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony upon testimony, explain its basis in istihsan, and identify the exception for hudud and qisas.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is allowed in all rights except hudud and qisas due to inherent doubt.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position on shahada ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony). You will learn why it is permitted despite strict qiyas, how istihsan operates as a proof, and why hudud and qisas are excluded. The passage from al-Hidayah provides the complete ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
First, locate the explicit ruling: testimony upon testimony is permissible (ja'iz) in every right that is not repelled by doubt. Note that 'right' (haqq) here includes financial claims, marriage, and property, but excludes hudud and qisas.
The phrase 'la yasquṭu bil-shubha' is key.
2
Understand the basis: istihsan
The text states 'hādha istiḥsān'. Recognize that istihsan is a departure from strict qiyas due to a stronger consideration. Here, the need (ḥāja) to preserve rights outweighs the objection from qiyas.
Istihsan is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the proof: severe need
The proof for istihsan is 'shiddat al-ḥāja ilayhā' (severe need). The original witness may be unable to testify due to illness, travel, or death. Without secondary testimony, rights would be lost.
This is the wajh al-dalāla linking need to permissibility.
4
Recognize the inherent doubt (shubha)
The text acknowledges that testimony upon testimony involves shubha: it is substitutional (badaliyya) and increases the probability of error. This shubha is why it is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
'Shubha' here means a factor that could lead to uncertainty.
5
Apply the exception
The final ruling: testimony upon testimony is not accepted in hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) because these are repelled by any doubt (shubha). In all other rights, it is permissible.
This exception is derived from the maxim 'al-ḥudūd tudra'u bi al-shubuhāt'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشهادة على الشهادة جائزة فى كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة وهذا استحسان لشدة الحاجة اليها اذ شاهد الاصل قد يعجز عن اداء الشهادة لبعض العوارض فلو لم يجز الشهادة على الشهادة ادى الى اتواء الحقوق ولهذا جوزنا الشهادة على الشهادة وان كثرت الا ان فيها شبهة من حيث البدلية او من حيث ان فيها زيادة احتمال وقد امكن الاحتراز عنه بجنس الشهود فلا تقبل فيما يندرىء بالشبهات كالحدود والقصاص
He said: Testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not invalidated by doubt, and this is istihsan due to the severe need for it, because the original witness may be unable to perform testimony due to some impediments. If testimony upon testimony were not permitted, it would lead to loss of rights. For this reason we have permitted testimony upon testimony even if numerous, except that there is doubt in it from the aspect of substitution or from the aspect that there is increased probability. And it is possible to avoid this by means of the type of witnesses, so it is not accepted in matters that are repelled by doubts, such as hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. The author states the Hanafi position that shahada ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony) is permissible (ja'iz) in every right that is not repelled by shubha (doubt). This ruling is based on istihsan, a form of jaryan al-qiyas, prioritizing necessity over strict analogy. The strict qiyas would reject it because testimony is a bodily act of worship (ibada badaniyya) that cannot be delegated. However, due to the severe need to protect people's rights from being lost when original witnesses are unable to attend (e.g., due to illness, travel), the Hanafi school adopts istihsan and allows it. The text notes that even if the chain of witnesses is long, it is accepted, but there is an inherent shubha because it is substitutional (badaliyya) and increases the possibility of falsehood. Since this shubha can be avoided by having the original witnesses themselves testify (by increasing their number), the practice is limited to rights that are not repelled by doubt. Therefore, shahada ala al-shahada is not accepted in hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) because those penalties are repelled by any doubt. This exception is crucial for Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony given by secondary witnesses based on the testimony of original witnesses, also known as shahada ala al-shahada.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling due to necessity or custom.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or uncertainty that can affect the validity of a ruling, specifically used here as a factor that repels hudud and qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following rights is shahada ala al-shahada NOT accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) Property disputes
B) Hudud penalties
C) Debt claims
D) Marriage contracts

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony is allowed in all rights except hudud and qisas due to the principle that penalties are repelled by doubts.

Number of Witnesses in Testimony upon Testimony
States the required number of witnesses in secondary testimony and responds to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required number of secondary witnesses for shahada ala al-shahada and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Two secondary witnesses suffice for two originals; the standard nisab applies to transmission of testimony.

When a witness is unavailable, Islamic law allows secondary testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). However, the required number of secondary witnesses is a point of dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi view that two secondary witnesses are sufficient for two original witnesses, and the Shafi'i objection that four are needed. We will follow the evidence and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the permissibility of shahada ala al-shahada: it is permissible for two secondary witnesses to testify on the testimony of two original witnesses. Note that the Hanafi school accepts this as valid.
This is a procedural ruling about the admissibility of evidence in court.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that two secondary witnesses are sufficient for two original witnesses. This is based on the hadith of Ali (ra) that the testimony of one man requires the testimony of two men. Also, transmitting testimony is a right (haqq), so the standard nisab (two witnesses) applies.
This means four witnesses total: two originals and two secondaries.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that four secondary witnesses are required for each pair of original witnesses. He analogizes each pair of secondary witnesses to a single witness (like one man) and then further analogizes to the case of two women replacing one man, requiring four women for two men. Hence, four secondaries for two originals.
This would require six witnesses total: two originals and four secondaries.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal relies on the direct hadith of Ali (ra) which shows that two men are sufficient for one original testimony. Furthermore, the transmission of testimony is a distinct right, not analogous to women's testimony. The nisab for rights is two witnesses, not one.
The Hanafis also note that their position is supported by a narration used against Imam Malik.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, four witnesses (two original, two secondary) are accepted; under Shafi'i, six witnesses are required. This affects the burden on the litigant who must produce secondary witnesses.
The Hanafi position is considered mufta bihi based on the strength of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز شهادة شاهدين على شهادة شاهدين وقال الشافعى لا يجوز الا الاربع على كل اصل اثنان لان كل شاهدين قائمان مقام شاهد واحد فصار كالمرأتين ولنا قول على رضى الله عنه لا يجوز على شهادة رجل الاشهادة رجلين ولان نقل شهادة الأصل من الحقوق فهما شهدا بحق ثم شهدا بحق آخر فتقبل ولا تقبل شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد لما روينا وهو حجة على مالك ولانه حق من الحقوق فلابد من نصاب الشهادة
And it is permissible for two witnesses to testify on the testimony of two witnesses. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible except four on each original two, because each two witnesses stand in the place of one witness, so it becomes like two women. And our proof is the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): It is not permissible regarding the testimony of one man except the testimony of two men. And because transmitting the testimony of the original is from among rights, so they testify concerning a right and then testify concerning another right, so it is accepted. And the testimony of one upon one is not accepted based on what we narrated, and it is proof against Malik. And because it is a right from among rights, so the nisab of testimony is required.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school holds that for shahada ala al-shahada, two secondary witnesses may testify upon the testimony of two original witnesses. This means that two secondary witnesses together constitute one full testimony upon one original witness pair. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that four secondary witnesses are required for each pair of original witnesses, because he analogizes each pair of secondary witnesses to a single witness (like one man or two women). The Hanafi response relies on the hadith of Imam Ali (ra) that the testimony of one man requires the testimony of two men, implying that two secondary witnesses are sufficient for one original. Additionally, the Hanafis argue that the transmission of testimony is a right (haqq) similar to other rights, so the standard nisab (two witnesses) applies. Therefore, one secondary witness upon one original witness is not accepted, as is also the position of Imam Malik according to the text. This dispute has practical implications: under Hanafi law, four witnesses total (two original + two secondary) are sufficient, while Shafi'i requires six (two original + four secondary).

Key Terms
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The required number of witnesses for a valid testimony; typically two men or one man and two women.
شاهد أصل (shahid asl): Original witness who directly observed or heard the event.
شاهد فرع (shahid far'): Secondary witness who testifies to the testimony of the original witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two secondary witnesses
C) Four secondary witnesses
D) Eight secondary witnesses

Key Takeaway
In shahada ala al-shahada, the Hanafi school requires two secondary witnesses for two original witnesses, relying on the direct hadith of Ali and applying the standard nisab.

Shahadat 'Ala al-Shahadat: The Hanafi Ruling and Istihsan Reasoning
Explaining the Hanafi ruling and istihsan reasoning for testimonial agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why shahadat 'ala al-shahadat is permitted by istihsan despite the qiyas objection, and state the scope of its application (rights not invalidated by doubt).

Core Idea
Shahadat 'ala al-shahadat is permitted by istihsan to preserve rights, not by qiyas.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on testimonial agency (shahadat 'ala al-shahadat). While qiyas would prohibit it because testimony is a bodily act of worship, the Hanafi school departs from qiyas and permits it by istihsan due to dire necessity. We will explore the reasoning behind both positions and the practical implications for preserving people's rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi ruling
What is shahadat 'ala al-shahadat? A secondary witness testifies to the original witness's testimony. The Hanafi ruling: it is ja'iz (permissible) by istihsan for any right that is not invalidated by doubt.
This is the conclusion stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Understand the qiyas counterargument
Why does qiyas say it is not permissible? Because testimony is a bodily act of worship (ibadah badaniyyah) incumbent on the original witness, and agency (niyabah) is not valid in bodily acts of worship. Thus, testimonial agency should be invalid.
The qiyas is based on the principle that bodily acts cannot be delegated.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
What grounds the departure from qiyas? Dire need (hajah shadidah): if original witnesses are unable to testify due to illness, travel, etc., rights would be lost. Preserving rights is obligatory, so istihsan permits testimonial agency despite qiyas.
Istihsan overrides qiyas when stronger considerations exist.
4
Examine the scope and limitations
The testimony of branches (furu') involves doubt (shubhah) because it is a substitute (badal) and the probability of falsehood increases. Therefore, it is not accepted in matters that are invalidated by doubt, such as hudud and qisas.
The ruling is limited to rights that are not invalidated by doubt.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
The Hanafi position is that shahadat 'ala al-shahadat is permissible regardless of the number of secondary witnesses, as long as the right survives doubt. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may impose stricter conditions, such as requiring a specific number of witnesses.
This ikhtilaf will be detailed in subsequent lessons.
