کیوں نہ ہو جائے ۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ فروع کی شہادت میں ایک گونہ شبہ ہے، شبہ یا تو اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ فروع اصول کے بدل ہیں اور بدل کی طرف اس وقت رجوع کیا جاتا جب انسان اصل سے عاجز ہو جائے اور یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔ یعنی شہادت فروع کیطرف، شہادت اصل سے بجز کے وقت رجوع کیا جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال شہادت فروع بدل ہے اور بدل میں اصل کی بہ نسبت ایک گونہ شبہ ہوتا ہے یا شہادت فروع میں اس اعتبار سے شبہ ہے کہ اس میں احتمال کذب زیادہ ہے، یعنی اصل گواہوں میں اُن کے معصوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے جھوٹ کا احتمال تھا لہذا فروع میں احتمال اور زیادہ ہو گا ۔ بہر حال شہادت فروع میں ایک گونہ شبہ ہے اور جنس شہود یعنی شہر داصل کے ذریعہ شہادت فروع سے بچنا بھی ممکن ہے اس طور پر کہ اصول کی تعداد زیادہ ہو۔ اگر بعض کو عذر پیش آگیا تو باقی دوسرے شہو د اصل گواہی دیدیں گے۔ بہر حال جب شہادت فرع میں شبہ ہے اور شہود اصل کے ذریعہ اس سے بچنا بھی ممکن ہے تو شہو د فرع کی شہادت ایسی چیزوں میں قبول نہ ہوگی جو چیزیں شبہات کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں ... جیسے حدود و قصاص ۔
The commentary of Sahib Quduri said: Testimony upon testimony is permitted by istihsan for every right that does not fall due to doubt, even if it is not permitted by qiyas. The basis of qiyas is that testimony is a bodily act of worship that is obligatory upon the original witness, and it is not a right of the defendant, because the defendant has the right to litigate against the witnesses, and not the right to compel testimony. In any case, testimony is a bodily act of worship and it is obligatory upon the original, and agency does not run in bodily acts of worship. Therefore, testimony upon testimony, which is agency, will also not run and will not be permissible. But to keep people's rights alive, qiyas is abandoned here. The basis of istihsan is that there is a dire need for testimony upon testimony, because sometimes the original witnesses become unable to perform testimony due to impediments. For example, if the original witnesses are sick, or traveling, or cannot go to the judge's court due to some engagement, then if testimony upon testimony is not permitted, people's rights would be destroyed, whereas destroying people's rights is not permissible and keeping them alive is obligatory. So due to this dire need, testimony upon testimony is deemed permissible, even if the secondary witnesses are many. The numerousness of secondary witnesses has two meanings: one is that the original witnesses appointed two witnesses as their deputies, then those deputies appointed their deputies, then they appointed their deputies, and so on. In this case, it will be in the meaning of 'even if they are many and distant.' The second meaning is that the original witnesses are two, each of them appointed two witnesses for his testimony, then each of the four secondary witnesses appointed two witnesses for his testimony; in this case 'even if they are many' remains in its meaning, and the meaning is that however many the secondary witnesses increase, it is permissible. Yes, it is essential that in the testimony of the branches there is some doubt. The doubt is either because the branches are substitutes for the originals, and substitution is resorted to only when one is incapable of the original, and here it is the same; that is, to the testimony of the branches, resort is made only when one is incapable of the original testimony. In any case, the testimony of the branches is a substitute, and a substitute has some doubt compared to the original. Or the doubt in the testimony of the branches is because the probability of falsehood is greater; that is, in the original witnesses there was a probability of falsehood because they are not infallible, so in the branches the probability increases. In any case, the testimony of the branches has some doubt, and it is also possible to avoid the testimony of the branches by means of a number of original witnesses, in that the originals are numerous; if some face an excuse, the remaining original witnesses will testify. In any case, when the testimony of the branches involves doubt and it is also possible to avoid it through original witnesses, then the testimony of the branches will not be accepted in things that are invalidated due to doubts... such as hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is an explanation from the commentary (sharh) of Quduri's text on shahadat 'ala al-shahadat (testimony upon testimony). The author first states the Hanafi ruling: it is permitted by istihsan (juristic preference) for any right that is not invalidated by doubt, even though qiyas (analogy) would not permit it. He then explains the qiyas argument: testimony is a purely bodily act of worship (ibadah badaniyyah) incumbent on the original witness, and the defendant has no right to compel testimony. Since agency (niyabah) is not valid in bodily acts of worship, testimonial agency should also be invalid. However, istihsan overrides qiyas due to necessity: if original witnesses are unable to testify due to illness, travel, or other excuses, rights would be lost, and preserving rights is obligatory. Therefore, shahadat 'ala al-shahadat is permitted. The author then discusses the two meanings of 'kathrah' (numerousness) of secondary witnesses: either a chain of deputies or each original appointing multiple deputies. He clarifies that the testimony of branches (furu') involves doubt (shubhah) because they are substitutes (badal) and because the probability of falsehood increases. Due to this doubt, such testimony is not accepted in matters that are invalidated by doubt, such as hudud and qisas. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi use of istihsan to address practical needs while maintaining legal principles.

Key Terms
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahadat 'ala al-shahadat): Testimony based on the testimony of another; a secondary witness testifies to the first witness's testimony rather than the original fact.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas (analogy) for a stronger reason, such as necessity or public interest.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a common effective cause ('illah).
شاہد اصل (shahid asl): The original witness who directly observed the event.
شاہد فرع (shahid far'): The secondary or deputy witness who testifies on behalf of the original witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, why is shahadat 'ala al-shahadat permitted despite qiyas against it?
A) Because it is an act of worship like prayer
B) Because of dire necessity to preserve people's rights
C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it
D) Because it is based on a consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
Shahadat 'ala al-shahadat is a Hanafi exception to qiyas, permitted by istihsan to safeguard rights when original witnesses cannot testify.

Number of Deputy Witnesses: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presenting the inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Malik on witness numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of deputy witnesses required for shahadat 'ala al-shahadat and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of textual preference over qiyas.

Core Idea
Two deputy witnesses suffice for two originals: the explicit word of Ali overrides qiyas.

This lesson explores a key inter-madhhab dispute in the law of testimony: how many deputy witnesses are needed to transmit the testimony of two original witnesses? The Hanafi school holds that two deputies are sufficient, while Imam al-Shafi'i requires four. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of a tradition from Ali (radi Allahu anhu) and the application of qiyas. Let's examine the proofs and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold about the number of deputy witnesses required for shahadat 'ala al-shahadat?
Two deputy witnesses suffice for two original witnesses; they transmit the testimony of both originals sequentially.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school objects and on what grounds? Identify the opposing school and their required number.
Imam al-Shafi'i requires four deputy witnesses: two for each original.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is their dalil? Examine the qiyas they use.
Shafi'i qiyas: two deputy witnesses stand in place of one original witness, like two women for one man; thus four deputies for two originals.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? What is their primary textual proof?
Hanafis cite the saying of Ali (radi Allahu anhu): 'لا يجوز على شهادة رجل إلا شهادة رجلين' which overrides qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings? How does this affect court proceedings?
Hanafi courts accept two deputies; Shafi'i courts require four, impacting convenience and procedural efficiency.

The Shar'i status of testimony upon testimony. And it is permissible for two witnesses to testify upon the testimony of two witnesses. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible except with four, for each original witness two, because every two (deputy) witnesses stand in place of one witness, so it becomes like two women. Our proof is the saying of 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'It is not permissible upon the testimony of a man except the testimony of two men.' And because the transmission of the original testimony is from among rights; thus they testified to a right, then they testified to another right, so it is accepted. And the testimony of one upon one is not accepted due to what we have narrated. And it is a proof against Malik. And because it is a right from among rights, so the required number of witnesses (nisab) is necessary. Translation: And the testimony of two witnesses upon the testimony of two witnesses is permissible. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with less than four; for each original witness, two witnesses, because every two deputy witnesses stand in place of one original witness, so it becomes like two women. And our proof is the saying of 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'It is not permissible upon the testimony of a man except the testimony of two men.' And because the transmission of the original testimony is from among rights; thus these two testified to a right, then these two testified to another right, so this testimony is accepted. And the testimony of one upon one is not accepted due to the hadith we have narrated. And it is a proof against Malik. And because the transmission of the original testimony is a right from among rights, therefore the required number of testimony is necessary. The commentary of Sahib Quduri said: According to us, the testimony of two deputy witnesses upon the testimony of two original witnesses is permissible; i.e., both deputy witnesses will first transmit the testimony of one original witness, then these same two will transmit the testimony of the other original witness. Thus two deputy witnesses can transmit the testimony of both original witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i said: To transmit the testimony of two original witnesses, four deputy witnesses are necessary: two deputies will transmit the testimony of one original witness, and the other two deputies will transmit the testimony of the other original witness. According to Imam Malik, one deputy witness is sufficient: i.e., one deputy witness will once transmit the testimony of one original witness, and once transmit the testimony of the other original witness. Thus one deputy witness suffices. Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni said: This is not the madhhab of Imam Malik; rather it could be one narration from him; his madhhab is the same as ours. Allamah Ibn al-Humann said likewise. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that two deputy witnesses stand in place of one original witness, just as two women stand in place of one man. So when two deputy witnesses stand in place of one original witness, then for the substitution of two original witnesses, four deputy witnesses are necessary. Imam Malik's proof is that the deputy witness is like a messenger (qasid) to convey the original witness's testimony to the court. So it is as if the original witness himself came to the court and testified; and if the original witnesses themselves testify, each testifies alone. Therefore, when a deputy witness conveys testimony on their behalf, he alone suffices; i.e., he will convey the testimony once, and then convey the other's testimony once. His second proof is qiyas: Imam Malik analogized the transmission of testimony to the narration of hadith. Just as in narrating hadith, the narration of one person from another is accepted, similarly, it is permissible for one person to transmit and narrate the testimony of one person. Our proof is the saying of 'Ali: 'It is not permissible upon the testimony of a man except the testimony of two men.' Meaning: two deputy witnesses should once transmit the testimony of one original witness and once transmit the testimony of the other original witness; thus each original witness will have two deputy witnesses, and the number of deputy witnesses will not increase from two to four, as the seasoned jurist Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah illuminate his grave, said.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of witnesses required for shahadat 'ala al-shahadat (testimony upon testimony). The Hanafi position is that two deputy witnesses can testify for both original witnesses; they first transmit the testimony of one original, then of the other, thus fulfilling the requirement of two witnesses for each original. Al-Shafi'i argues that each original witness requires two deputy witnesses, so four deputies are needed, analogizing to the rule that two women stand in place of one man in testimony. Imam Malik is reported to hold that one deputy suffices, analogizing to hadith narration where one narrator transmits from another. However, the commentary notes that according to 'Ayni and Ibn al-Humann, this is not Malik's established view; his school agrees with the Hanafis. The Hanafi proof is the saying of 'Ali (radi Allahu anhu) that the testimony of a man requires two men, implying that two deputies can cover both originals. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the required number (nisab) of testimony must be met, and that the deputy witnesses' testimony is accepted as a valid right. This discussion highlights the importance of preserving the integrity of testimony while accommodating practical needs.

Key Terms
نصاب الشہادہ (nisab al-shahadah): The required number of witnesses for testimony to be accepted; in this context, the number of deputy witnesses needed.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Standing in place of; deputyship; used to describe how deputy witnesses replace original witnesses.
حضرت علی کا قول (Hadhrat 'Ali ka qawl): The saying of 'Ali (radi Allahu anhu) used as proof for the Hanafi position: 'لا يجوز على شهادة رجل إلا شهادة رجلين'.
قاصد (qasid): A messenger; used by Malik's alleged view to describe the deputy witness as a mere conveyor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Two deputy witnesses are sufficient for shahadat 'ala al-shahadat in the Hanafi school, based on the explicit statement of 'Ali (radi Allahu anhu) that overrides qiyas.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Number of Witnesses for Testimony upon Testimony (Shahada ala al-Shahada)
Inter-madhhab dispute on nisab of secondary witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the required number of secondary witnesses for testimony upon testimony, compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki views, and evaluate the proofs each school uses.

Core Idea
Two secondary witnesses suffice for two original witnesses because each transfer of testimony is a separate right requiring its own nisab.

This lesson explores an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of secondary witnesses needed to testify to the testimony of two original witnesses. The Hanafi school holds that two secondary witnesses can sequentially testify for both originals, while the Shafi'is require four and Malikis accept one. Understanding the proofs behind each position sharpens your ability to analyze evidentiary rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The central question is: how many secondary witnesses are needed to establish the testimony of two original witnesses in a financial claim? The answer determines the validity of testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada).
The nisab (minimum number) for direct testimony in financial matters is two men or one man and two women.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Primary Proof
Hanafis say two secondary witnesses can testify to both original witnesses sequentially. Their proof is the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'لا يجوز على شهادة رجل الا شهادة رجلین' (testimony on the testimony of one man is not permissible except with two men). This directly requires two men for each original testimony.
The phrase 'لا يجوز' indicates prohibition of accepting less than two.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Position and Its Analogy
Shafi'is argue that two secondary witnesses are equivalent to one original witness, just as two women equal one man. Therefore, for two originals, four secondary witnesses are needed.
This analogy is central to the Shafi'i argument and is critiqued by Hanafis.
4
Examine the Maliki Position and Its Analogies
Malikis (according to one narration) hold that one secondary witness suffices because he is like a messenger conveying testimony. They also analogize to hadith narration, where one narrator can transmit from another.
Some Hanafi commentators dispute whether this is the established Maliki view.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response to Each Opposing Proof
Hanafis respond: (1) Ali's statement explicitly requires two, overriding the women analogy; (2) Each transfer is a separate right, and two witnesses can testify to multiple rights sequentially; (3) Two women do not fulfill nisab, but here two secondary witnesses do; (4) Hadith narration is not a 'right' (haqq) and does not require nisab.
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the transfer of testimony is a right of the people (haqq min huquq al-nas), which requires full nisab.

Source Text

Translation: And it is permissible to have two witnesses on the testimony of two witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i said that less than four is not permissible: for each original witness there are two witnesses, because each two secondary witnesses are in place of one original witness, thus they become like two women. And our proof is the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Testimony on the testimony of one man is not permissible except with two men.' And because transferring the testimony of the original is among rights. So these two first gave testimony for the first right, then these same two gave testimony for the second right, so this testimony is accepted. And the testimony of one is not accepted on one due to the Hadith we have narrated. And this is an argument against Imam Malik. And because transferring the original testimony is one right, so completion of the required number of witnesses (nisab) is necessary. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that according to us, testimony of two secondary witnesses on the testimony of two original witnesses is permissible, meaning both secondary witnesses will first transfer the testimony of one original witness, then these same two will transfer the testimony of the other original witness. Thus two secondary witnesses can transfer the testimony of both original witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i said that to transfer the testimony of two original witnesses, four secondary witnesses are necessary: two secondary witnesses will transfer the testimony of one original witness, and the other two secondary witnesses will transfer the testimony of the other original witness. According to Imam Malik, one secondary witness is sufficient: one secondary witness will once transfer the testimony of one original witness and once transfer the testimony of the other original witness. Thus one secondary witness suffices. Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni said that this is not the madhhab of Malik; rather it may be a narration from him; his madhhab is the same as ours. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said the same. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that two secondary witnesses are in place of one original witness, just as two women are in place of one man. So when two secondary witnesses are in place of one original witness, then for representation of two original witnesses, four secondary witnesses are necessary. Imam Malik's proof is that the secondary witness is like a messenger to convey the original witness's testimony to the court. So it is as if the original witness himself testified before the judge, and if the original witnesses testified themselves, each would testify alone. Therefore, when the secondary witness transfers testimony on their behalf, he alone is sufficient: he will transfer testimony once and once transfer the testimony of the other. The second proof is qiyas: Imam Malik analogizes the transfer of testimony to the narration of hadith. Just as in narrating hadith, one person's narration from one person is accepted, similarly one person's transferring and narrating one person's testimony is permissible. Our proof is the statement of Ali: 'Testimony on the testimony of one man is not permissible except with two men.' Meaning two secondary witnesses will once transfer the testimony of one original witness and once transfer the testimony of the other original witness, thus each original witness's testimony has two secondary witnesses, and the number of secondary witnesses will not exceed two to four. As the faqih and spiritual master Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah illuminate his grave) said. The second proof is that transferring the original witness's testimony is among the rights of people, and to establish that right, the required number of witnesses (two) is necessary. So when two secondary witnesses transferred the testimony of one original witness, they gave testimony for one right and the required number was fulfilled; then when these same secondary witnesses transferred the testimony of the other original witness, they gave testimony for a second right besides the first, and the required number was also fulfilled for it. And it is accepted that two witnesses can give testimony for different rights one after another. So when each original witness's testimony was transferred with the required number, the testimony of these two secondary witnesses will be accepted. Unlike the testimony of two women, because two women are in the rank of one man, so two women do not fulfill the required number. And when the required number is not fulfilled by two women, the judge's verdict based on their testimony will not be established. The author of al-Hidayah gave the proof for non-acceptance of one secondary witness's testimony for one original witness from what we narrated, saying that the statement of Ali is a proof against Imam Malik because it explicitly states that two secondary witnesses are necessary to transfer the testimony of one original witness, while Imam Malik considers one sufficient. The rational argument against Malik is that transfer of testimony is a type of right, and to establish any right, the required number of witnesses is necessary. Therefore, to transfer the original witness's testimony, two secondary witnesses are necessary; one secondary witness will not suffice. As our great Imam Malik's statement is. Contrary to narrating hadith, because it is not among rights, so one person can narrate from one person.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of secondary witnesses required to testify to the testimony of two original witnesses. The author states the Hanafi position first: it is permissible to have two secondary witnesses for two original witnesses; they both testify to the first, then both to the second. This is based on the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) that the testimony of one man cannot be established by another's testimony except with two men. The Hanafi argument is that transferring testimony is a right, and each right requires its own full set of witnesses (nisab). Thus, two secondary witnesses can sequentially transfer two rights. The Shafi'i position holds that since two secondary witnesses equal one original witness (like two women equal one man), for two original witnesses four secondary witnesses are needed. The Maliki position, as reported, holds that one secondary witness suffices because he is like a messenger; the original witnesses would have testified individually, so their deputy can do the same. Additionally, Malik analogizes to hadith narration where one person can narrate from another. The Hanafi response counters with the explicit proof from Ali's statement and the logic that each transfer is a separate right requiring its own nisab. The commentary from Sharh al-Hidayah and others clarifies that the reported Maliki view may not be his established madhhab but a rare narration. The passage also distinguishes this from testimony of two women, which does not fulfill the nisab because two women equal one man in testimony.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony, where secondary witnesses testify to the testimony of primary witnesses.
شاهد أصل (shahid asl): Original witness who directly witnessed the event.
شاهد فرع (shahid far'): Secondary witness who testifies to the testimony of the original witness.
نصاب شهادة (nisab al-shahada): The minimum number of witnesses required to establish a right; for financial claims, two men or one man and two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many secondary witnesses are required to testify to the testimony of two original witnesses?
A) Four secondary witnesses (two for each original)
B) Two secondary witnesses who testify sequentially to both originals
C) One secondary witness who can testify to both originals
D) Three secondary witnesses

Key Takeaway
Two secondary witnesses are sufficient for two original witnesses in testimony upon testimony, based on the explicit statement of Ali and the principle that each transfer of testimony is a separate right requiring its own nisab.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
10 min
Procedure for Making a Witness on Testimony
Description of the proper wording for making a secondary witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct wording for an original witness to commission a secondary witness and identify the conditions under which the testimony is valid.

Core Idea
The original witness must formally commission the secondary as a deputy, but mere hearing of a confession suffices for validity.

In Islamic legal procedure, testimony (shahada) is a crucial means of proof. When an original witness cannot be present, they may commission a secondary witness to convey their testimony. This lesson explains the exact wording required for this commissioning and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors
Determine who is the original witness (shahid al-asl) and who is the secondary witness (shahid al-far'). Understand their relationship.
2
Analyze the required wording
The original must say a phrase like 'I call you to witness upon my testimony that I testify that...' This establishes the secondary as a deputy.
The phrase includes 'ashhad 'ala shahadati' or similar.
3
Understand the rationale
The secondary is a deputy (na'ib) of the original; thus, formal commissioning (tahmil) and authorization (tawkil) are necessary.
This ensures the testimony is traceable.
4
Identify the manner of testifying
The original must testify as he would before the judge, so that the secondary can accurately convey it to the court.
5
Recognize the leniency
If the original does not say 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi', the secondary's testimony is still valid because anyone who hears a confession may testify.
This is a relaxation of the strict wording requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہادت پر گواہ بنانے کا طریقہ
وصفة الاشهاد ان يقول شاهد الاصل لشاهد الفرع اشهد على شهادتى انى اشهد ان فلان ابن فلان اقر عندى بكذا او اشهدنى على نفسه لان الفرع كالنائب عنه فلابد من التحميل والتوكيل على ما مر ولابد ان يشهد كما يشهد عند القاضى لينقله الى مجلس القضاء وان لم يقل اشهدنى على نفسه جاز لان من سمع اقرار غيره حل له الشهادة وان لم يقل له اشهد
ترجمہ اور اپنی گواہی پر گواہ پر گواہ کرنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ شاہد اصل، شاہد فرع سے یوں کہے کہ تو میری شہادت پر شہادت دے کہ میں شہادت دیتا ہوں کہ فلاں بن فلاں نے میرے پاس ایسا ایسا اقرار کیا ہے اور مجھے اپنی ذات پر شاہد کر لیا ہے اس لئے کہ فرعی گواہ گویا اصلی گواہ کا نائب ہے۔ پس گواہی لا دنا اور وکیل بنانا ضروری ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذرا ۔ اور ضروری ہے کہ اصلی گواہ اسی طرح شہادت دے جیسے قاضی کے پاس شہادت دیتا ہے تا کہ شاہد فرع اس کو قاضی کی مجلس میں منتقل کرے اور اگر اصلی گواہ نے اشہد فی علی نفسہ نہ کہا ہوتو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ جس شخص نے دوسرے کا اقرار سنا اس کے لئے گواہی دینا حلال ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ مقر یاد گی علیہ نے اس سے اشہد نہ کیا ہو۔ تشریح شاہد اصل کا شاہد فرع کو اپنی شہادت پر گواہ کرنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ شاہد اصل شاہد فرع سے یوں کہے کہ میں شہادت دیتا ہوں
The manner of making a witness on testimony: The description of the procedure is that the original witness says to the secondary witness: 'I call you to witness upon my testimony that I testify that so-and-so son of so-and-so made a confession before me of such-and-such, or he made me a witness over himself.' Because the secondary is like a deputy for him, so commissioning and authorization are necessary as previously mentioned. And it is necessary that he testify as he would testify before the judge, so that the secondary can convey it to the court. If he does not say 'he made me a witness over himself,' it is still permissible, because whoever hears someone else's confession is permitted to testify, even if the confessor did not say 'make me a witness.' Explanation: The manner of the original witness making the secondary witness a witness on his testimony is that the original witness says to the secondary witness: 'I testify...'
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage describes the specific wording required for making a secondary witness on testimony (al-ishhad). The original witness must formally commission the secondary witness by saying 'I call you to witness upon my testimony that I testify...' This establishes the secondary witness as a deputy (na'ib) of the original, necessary to transfer the testimony. The passage notes that if the original does not explicitly say 'he made me a witness,' the testimony is still valid because anyone who hears a confession can testify. The commentary explains that the secondary must testify in the same manner as before the judge. The text ends abruptly, but it indicates that the original witness says 'I testify' to commission the secondary.

Key Terms
تحميل (tahmil): The act of the original witness formally burdening the secondary witness with the duty to testify.
توكيل (tawkil): Authorization: the original witness appointing the secondary as a deputy to convey testimony.
اشهدنى على نفسه (ashhadani 'ala nafsihi): A phrase meaning 'he made me a witness over himself,' indicating that the original witness was explicitly called to witness a confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The original must say 'اشهدنى على نفسه'
B) The original must explicitly say 'اشهد على شهادتى'
C) The original must say a formal commissioning phrase, but if he does not, the secondary's testimony is still valid if he heard the original's confession
D) The secondary must request the commission in writing

Key Takeaway
The commissioning of a secondary witness requires explicit wording, but the absence of the phrase 'اشهدنى على نفسه' does not invalidate the testimony if the secondary heard the confession.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Conditions and Wording for Secondary Testimony
Explains condition of tahmil and recommended wording for shahadah 'ala al-shahadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of tahmil for secondary testimony and apply the recommended wording for delivering such testimony in court.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony requires explicit delegation (tahmil) from the original witness; without it, the testimony is invalid.

The Hanafi school has detailed rules for shahadah 'ala al-shahadah (testimony on testimony). This lesson explains the essential condition of tahmil: the original witness must explicitly ask the secondary witness to bear witness on his testimony. Additionally, it covers the recommended wording for the secondary witness when delivering the testimony in court, based on the principle 'khayr al-umur awsatuha' (the best of matters is the middle course).

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational condition
The original witness must delegate (tahmil) the testimony to the secondary witness by saying 'ashhad 'ala shahadati' or similar. This is wajib for validity.
2
Understand the rationale
The secondary witness acts as an agent (na'ib) of the original in conveying the testimony; agency requires explicit appointment.
3
Analyze the subtle nuance
Al-Hidayah says 'ka al-na'ib' (like a deputy) rather than 'na'ibuhu' because the secondary is a deputy in the subject matter, not in the act of testifying itself.
4
Examine the recommended wording
The secondary witness should state: 'I bear witness that so-and-so made me a witness on his testimony that so-and-so confessed... and he told me: be a witness on my testimony.' This includes the necessary elements.
5
Note the flexibility
Longer or shorter phrases are permissible, but the intermediate wording from al-Quduri is preferred based on the maxim 'khayr al-umur awsatuha'.

Chapter of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume 10. ... And the condition that the original witness makes the secondary witness a witness over his testimony is because the secondary witness is like the deputy of the original witness, and making someone a deputy is necessary; without being made a deputy, no one can be a deputy. Therefore, it is necessary for the original witness to make the secondary witness testify on his testimony. Also, testimony on testimony is only valid when the secondary witness transfers the testimony of the original witness to the judge in the court, and the secondary witness is only authorized to transfer it at that time when the original witness has placed the burden of testimony upon him. In any case, it is established that for testimony on testimony, tahmil (delegation) is required, i.e., the original witness saying 'be witness on my testimony' and thus making him a bearer of testimony, and since the secondary witness is the agent of the original witness, it is also necessary to make him an agent. The detail has passed in the section on 'what the witness bears'. But the question is: when the secondary witness is the deputy of the original witness, why did the author of al-Hidayah say 'because the secondary is like his deputy' rather than 'because the secondary is his deputy'? The answer is that the secondary witness is not his deputy in his testimony but rather is a deputy in the testified matter; therefore he said 'like a deputy'. The author of al-Hidayah said: The original witness should testify before the secondary witness in the same way he would testify before the judge, so that the secondary witness, having heard from the original, can transfer exactly to the judge's court. That is, as the original states, the secondary will convey it to the judge's court. And if the original witness did not say to the secondary witness that the confronter made me a witness over himself, it is still permissible, because a person who hears another's confession is allowed to testify, even if the confronter did not say 'be witness over myself'. The method of testifying on testimony: And the secondary witness, at the time of delivering testimony, says: 'I bear witness that so-and-so made me a witness on his testimony that so-and-so confessed before him for such-and-such amount and he told me: be a witness on my testimony regarding that.' Because his testimony is necessary, and mentioning the testimony of the original and mentioning the delegation are necessary. This phrase has a longer and shorter form, and the best of matters is the middle course. Translation: And when delivering testimony, the secondary witness says: I bear witness that such a person made me a witness on his testimony that such a person confessed before the original witness for such right, and the original witness said to me: be a witness on my testimony. Because the secondary witness's testimony is necessary, and mentioning the original witness's testimony and mentioning his making the secondary a witness is also necessary, and for secondary testimony, a longer or shorter phrase than the above is also permissible, and in matters the middle is best. Commentary: Al-Quduri stated describing the quality of the secondary witness's testimony: the secondary witness at the time of delivering testimony in the judge's court says: I bear witness that so-and-so son of so-and-so made me a witness on his testimony that so-and-so son of so-and-so confessed before him for the right of so-and-so son of so-and-so, and he said to me: be my witness on my testimony. The author of al-Hidayah says that the reason for saying this full phrase is that the secondary witness's testimony is necessary, so he says 'I give testimony.' And it is also necessary that the secondary witness mention the placing of the burden of testimony upon himself, so he says: the original witness said to me: be a witness on my testimony. The author of al-Hidayah said that at the time of delivery, the secondary witness can achieve his purpose with a longer phrase than the above or a shorter phrase. A longer phrase, for example: the secondary witness says before the judge: I bear witness that so-and-so gave testimony before me that so-and-so owes such-and-such to so-and-so, and he made me a witness on his testimony and commanded me to testify on his testimony, so I now testify on his testimony. And a shorter phrase, for example: the secondary witness says before the judge: I testify on the testimony of so-and-so regarding such-and-such. And the phrase mentioned in al-Quduri is intermediate, neither lengthy nor brief, and the rule 'the best of matters is the middle course' is well-known, so abandoning both long and short, this phrase was chosen.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the conditions and method for shahadah 'ala al-shahadah (testimony on testimony). The author first establishes the fundamental condition: the original witness (shahid asl) must explicitly delegate the testimony to the secondary witness (shahid far') by saying 'ashhad 'ala shahadati' (be witness on my testimony). This is because the secondary witness acts as an agent (na'ib) of the original in conveying the testimony, and agency must be established. The text then clarifies a subtle point: the author of al-Hidayah uses the phrase 'like a deputy' (ka al-na'ib) rather than 'deputy' because the secondary is not a deputy in the act of testifying itself but rather in the subject matter of the testimony (mashhud bihi). Next, the original witness is instructed to testify before the secondary witness exactly as before the judge, so that the secondary can reproduce it faithfully. Following this, the wording of the secondary witness when delivering testimony is given: he must state that the original made him a witness on his testimony, mention the underlying confession, and mention the delegation. The text then notes that longer or shorter formulations are permissible, but the intermediate wording from al-Quduri (based on the principle 'khayr al-umur awsatuha') is recommended as the best balance. The commentary also addresses that if the original did not mention that the confronter made him a witness over himself, it remains valid, as the act of delegation only concerns the transfer of testimony, not the confronter's appointment.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahadah 'ala al-shahadah): Testimony based on the testimony of another witness, where the secondary witness reports the original witness's testimony.
شاهد أصل (shahid asl): The original witness who directly witnessed the event or heard the confession.
شاهد فرع (shahid far'): The secondary witness who reports the testimony of the original witness.
تحميل (tahmil): The act of the original witness delegating the testimony to the secondary witness by saying 'ashhad 'ala shahadati'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for the original witness (shahid asl) to make the secondary witness (shahid far') valid?
A) He must say 'I bear witness that...'
B) He must say 'Be witness on my testimony' (ashhad 'ala shahadati)
C) He must write a document
D) He must have two witnesses present

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony in Hanafi law is valid only if the original witness explicitly delegates (tahmil) the testimony, and the secondary witness delivers it using wording that mentions the delegation and the underlying fact.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Requirement of Explicit Tahmil for Secondary Testimony
Resolves whether 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi' suffices for secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that explicit delegation (tahmil) is wajib for secondary testimony and explain the difference in rationale between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Without explicit 'ashhad 'ala shahadati', a listener cannot become a secondary witness.

This passage resolves a key ambiguity: does hearing 'he made me a witness over himself' authorize secondary testimony? The Hanafi school unanimously says no—explicit delegation is wajib. But the reasoning behind this requirement differs between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn, revealing deeper principles about proof transfer and liability.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify that a witness (original) says 'So-and-so made me a witness over himself'. A listener hears this and wants to testify as a secondary witness. The ruling: the listener cannot testify unless the original says 'Be a witness on my testimony'.
This is the core mas'alah.
2
Identify the agreed ruling
Both Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) agree that explicit tahmil is required for secondary testimony. There is no dispute on the outcome.
3
Contrast the rationales
Imam Muhammad bases the requirement on shared liability (daman) upon retraction: both original and secondary witness share responsibility, so delegation must be explicit. The Sahibayn base it on the necessity of transferring the original testimony to become a proof (hujja); delegation is the means of transfer.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is identical.
4
Apply the ruling to a new example
Given a scenario where a person only says 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi', determine that the listener is not authorized to testify until the original witness makes an explicit delegation.

اشهدنی فلان على نفسه سے سامع گواہی دے سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟
ومن قال اشهدني فلان على نفسه لم يشهد السامع على شهادته حتى يقول اشهد على شهادتي لانه لابد من التحميل وهذا ظاهر عند محمد لان القضاء عنده بشهادة الفروع والاصول جميعا حتى اشتركوا فى الضمان عند الرجوع وكذا عندهما لأنه لابد من نقل شهادة الاصول التصير حجة فيظهر تحميل ما هو حجة
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے کہا کہ فلاں نے مجھے اپنی ذات پر گواہ کیا ہے سامع اس کی گواہی پر گواہی نہ دے یہاں تک کہ اصلی گواہ یوں نہ کہے کہ تو میری گواہی پر گواہ ہو جا اس لئے کہ گواہی لا دنا ضروری ہے اور یہ امام محمد کے نزدیک ظاہر ہے کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک قاضی کا حکم دینا فروع اور اصول دونوں کی شہادت سے ہوتا ہے حتی کہ رجوع کے وقت دونوں فریق تاوان میں شریک ہوتے ہیں اور ایسے ہی شیخین کے نزدیک کیونکہ اصول کی شہادت نقل کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ حجت ہو جائے۔ پس جو چیز حجت ہے اس کا لا دنا ضروری ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شاہد مثلاً عارف نے کہا کہ فلاں مثلاً واصف نے اپنی ذات پر مجھ کو گواہ بنایا ہے اور ایک شخص مثلا خالد نے گواہ یعنی عارف کے اس قول کو سنا تو خالد ، شاہد فرع بن کر شاہد اصل (عارف) کی گواہی پر گواہی دینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر شاہد اصل (عارف) شاہد فرع (خالد) سے یہ کہے کہ تو میری گواہی پر گواہ ہو جا تو پھر شاہد فرع (خالد) کے لئے شہادت علی الشہادت کا جواز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت علی الشہادت کے لئے تحمیل بالا تفاق ضروری ہے امام محمد کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ شاہد فرع کو حق یعنی مشہود بہ کا کوئی علم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ وہ تو شاہد اصل کی شہادت کو اس کا وکیل بن کر مجلس قاضی کی طرف منتقل کرتا ہے اور قاضی اصول و فروع دونوں کی شہادت پر حکم صادر کرتا ہے چنانچہ اگر اصول و فروع دونوں نے شہادت سے رجوع کر لیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک تاوان میں دونوں فریق شریک ہوں گے دونوں کے شریک ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہرگز نہیں ہے کہ نصف تاوان کا فیصلہ اصول پر کیا جائیگا اور نصف کا فیصلہ فروع پر کیا جائے گا بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ مشہود علیہ کو اختیار ہوگا کہ وہ اصول سے تاوان کا مطالبہ کرے یا فروع سے تاوان کا مطالبہ کرے جیسے غاصب سے اگر شی مخصوص کو ضبط لیا گیا تو مغصوب منہ کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ وہ غاصب سے تاوان کا مطالبہ کرے یا غاصب الغاصب سے تاوان کا مطالبہ کرے بہر حال امام محمد کے نزدیک شاہد فرع ، وکیل بن کر
Whether the listener can give testimony from 'he made me a witness over himself'? And whoever said: So-and-so made me a witness over himself, the listener does not testify on his testimony until he says 'be witness on my testimony', because delegation is necessary, and this is apparent according to Muhammad because the judgment according to him is based on the testimony of both the secondary and original witnesses, such that they share in the indemnity upon retraction, and likewise according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because it is necessary to transfer the testimony of the originals to become a proof, so delegation of what is a proof is apparent. Translation: If someone said that so-and-so made me a witness over himself, the listener should not testify on his testimony until the original witness says 'you be a witness on my testimony', because delegation of testimony is necessary, and this is apparent according to Imam Muhammad because according to Imam Muhammad, the judge's verdict is based on the testimony of both the original and secondary witnesses, such that at the time of retraction both parties share in the indemnity. And similarly according to the two (Shaykhayn) because it is necessary to transfer the testimony of the original to become a proof, so delegating what is a proof is necessary. Commentary: The scenario is this: A witness, for example 'Arif, said that 'Wasif made me a witness over himself, and a person, for example Khalid, heard the witness, meaning 'Arif's statement. Then Khalid, as a secondary witness, is not authorized to give testimony on the testimony of the original witness ('Arif). However, if the original witness ('Arif) says to the secondary witness (Khalid) 'you be a witness on my testimony', then it is permissible for the secondary witness (Khalid) to give testimony on testimony. The proof is that for testimony on testimony, delegation (tahmil) is necessary by agreement. According to Imam Muhammad, this is because the secondary witness has no knowledge of the right (the testified matter); rather he transfers the testimony of the original witness as his agent to the judge's court, and the judge issues judgment based on the testimony of both original and secondary. Thus, if both original and secondary retract their testimony, then according to Imam Muhammad, both parties share in the indemnity. The meaning of both sharing is by no means that half the indemnity is assigned to the original and half to the secondary; rather the meaning is that the person against whom the testimony was given (mashhud 'alayhi) has the option to demand indemnity from the original or from the secondary. Similarly, if from a usurper a specific thing is taken, the one from whom it was usurped (maghsud minhu) has the option to demand indemnity from the usurper or from the sub-usurper. In any case, according to Imam Muhammad, the secondary witness, acting as an agent...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific mas'alah: if someone says 'ashhadani fulan 'ala nafsihi' (so-and-so made me a witness over his own right/obligation), can a third party (listener) give testimony on that testimony? The ruling is clear: no, because explicit delegation (tahmil) is required. The original witness must say 'ashhad 'ala shahadati' (be witness on my testimony). The text then provides the legal reasoning for this requirement, noting differences between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Imam Muhammad, since the judge's verdict relies on both the original and secondary witnesses' testimonies, and they share liability (daman) if they retract, the delegation is necessary to establish the secondary's role. According to the Sahibayn, the testimony of the original must be transferred to become a proof (hujja), so delegating that proof is necessary. The commentary gives a hypothetical example using 'Arif (original witness), Wasif (the person who made the original a witness over himself), and Khalid (prospective secondary witness) to illustrate that without explicit delegation, Khalid cannot testify. Once 'Arif says 'be witness on my testimony', Khalid may do so. The text also clarifies a point about shared liability: it does not mean half-half, but that the accused may choose to claim indemnity from either the original or the secondary. The passage ends abruptly on page 127, but the main ruling and reasoning are complete.

Key Terms
اشهدني على نفسه (ashhadani 'ala nafsihi): He made me a witness over himself (i.e., he appointed me as a witness to his own right or obligation).
اشهد على شهادتي (ashhad 'ala shahadati): Be a witness on my testimony; the required phrase for delegation (tahmil) from original witness to secondary.
ضمان (daman): Liability or indemnity that the original and secondary witnesses share if they retract their testimony.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony by a witness, leading to potential liability for false testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because Y heard X's statement directly
B) No, because explicit delegation (tahmil) is required
C) Yes, if there is another witness corroborating
D) No, only if X retracts

Key Takeaway
Explicit delegation ('ashhad 'ala shahadati') is wajib for secondary testimony; mere 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi' is insufficient in Hanafi law.

Requirement of Tahmil for Secondary Witnesses
Determines when a secondary witness may testify upon hearing 'ashhadani'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the requirement of tahmil for secondary witnesses and distinguish the reasoning of Imam Muhammad from that of the Shaykhayn.

Core Idea
A secondary witness cannot testify until explicitly loaded by the primary witness.

When a person hears another say 'ashhadani' (he testified me), that alone does not authorize the listener to testify as a secondary witness. The Hanafi school requires explicit tahmil—the primary witness must say 'ishhad 'ala shahadati' (be a witness upon my testimony). This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi reasoning behind this requirement, comparing Imam Muhammad's wakala-based view with the Shaykhayn's transmission-based view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed condition.
The act is the testimony of a secondary witness (shuhud al-furu'). The condition in dispute is whether explicit wording (tahmil) is required from the primary witness.
2
State the Hanafi position that tahmil is required.
Both Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn agree that the secondary witness cannot testify without the primary saying 'ishhad 'ala shahadati' or similar.
The disagreement is not about the requirement itself but the legal nature of the relationship.
3
Explain Imam Muhammad's reasoning (secondary as wakil).
Imam Muhammad views the secondary witness as an agent (wakil) of the primary. The primary's tahmil appoints the secondary as a representative to convey testimony. Thus, both testimonies are treated together, and they share liability if they retract.
Under this view, if the primary revokes the agency, the secondary can no longer testify.
4
Explain the Shaykhayn's reasoning (transmission needed).
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not consider the secondary as a wakil. Instead, they require tahmil because the primary's testimony must be transmitted to the court to become a valid proof. The secondary acts as a vehicle for that transmission.
Under this view, revocation of tahmil does not prevent testimony because no agency exists.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
If the primary witness forbids the secondary from testifying after giving tahmil: according to Imam Muhammad, the secondary cannot testify (wakala ends); according to the Shaykhayn, he can (transmission is already completed).
This difference affects fatwa but both agree tahmil is initially necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال اشهدني فلان على نفسه لم يشهد السامع على شهادته حتى يقول اشهد على شهادتي لانه لابد من التحميل وهذا ظاهر عند محمد لان القضاء عنده بشهادة الفروع والاصول جميعا حتى اشتركوا فى الضمان عند الرجوع وكذا عندهما لأنه لابد من نقل شهادة الاصول التصير حجة فيظهر تحميل ما هو حجة
And whoever says, 'So-and-so testified me against himself,' the listener does not testify upon his testimony until he says, 'Testify upon my testimony,' because tahmil is necessary. And this is evident according to Muhammad, because according to him the judge's ruling is based on the testimony of both the branches and the roots, such that they share in the liability upon retraction. And similarly according to them (the two seniors), because it is necessary to transmit the testimony of the roots to become a proof, so tahmil of that which is a proof appears.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of tahmil (loading) for secondary witnesses (shuhud al-furu'). The primary witness (shahid al-asl) must say to the secondary witness, 'Be a witness upon my testimony' or similar, for the secondary to be able to testify. Imam Muhammad's reasoning is that he considers the secondary witness as an agent (wakil) of the primary, so the ruling is based on both testimonies, and they share liability if they retract. The two seniors (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) also require tahmil but for a different reason: the primary's testimony needs to be transmitted to become a proof, and tahmil is needed for that transmission. The passage clarifies that even though the two seniors do not consider the secondary as a wakil, they still require tahmil because the transmission of the primary's testimony to the court is necessary for it to be a valid proof.

Key Terms
شهود الفروع (shuhud al-furu'): Secondary witnesses who testify based on the testimony of primary witnesses.
تحميل (tahmil): The act of the primary witness instructing the secondary to testify on his behalf.
وكيل (wakil): Agent; according to Imam Muhammad, the secondary witness acts as an agent of the primary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a secondary witness to testify according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hearing the primary witness say 'ashhadani'
B) The primary witness saying 'ishhad 'ala shahadati'
C) The death of the primary witness
D) The secondary witness being present at the original event

Key Takeaway
Tahmil is a necessary condition for secondary witness testimony in the Hanafi school, regardless of the underlying reasoning.

Conditions for Accepting Secondary Witness Testimony
Lists three conditions for accepting secondary testimony: death, absence, sickness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the three conditions for accepting secondary testimony and EXPLAIN the rationale of necessity (haja) that justifies the exception.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is exceptional, allowed only when primary witnesses are truly incapacitated.

Secondary testimony (shahadat al-furu') is a departure from the normal procedure where original witnesses must testify in person. The Hanafi school permits this exception strictly based on necessity (haja). In this lesson, we examine the three classical conditions and an additional view from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exception
The author states the general rule: secondary testimony is not accepted. Then lists exceptions. Recognize that the default is prohibition; only under specific conditions is it permitted. The exception is based on necessity (haja).
2
List the three standard conditions
Memorize these three: death, absence for three days or more, illness preventing attendance. They are the mufta bihi.
The travel condition is measured by three days, a legal standard used elsewhere.
3
Analyze the rationale: why these conditions?
The text explains that incapacity ('ajz) is realized through these. Understand the underlying illa: inability of the primary witness to attend court. These three are objective indicators of impossibility. Qiyas: necessity permits the exception.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf adds a fourth scenario: inability to return home same day. Compare the two views. Abu Yusuf broadens the condition to include shorter travel that still prevents a same-day return.
This is based on the same illa of genuine hardship.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The scholars say first is better, second is more appropriate; Abu al-Layth adopted the second. The mufta bihi is the first, but the second is applied when it serves the purpose of necessity. Tarjih is not absolute; context matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا تقبل شهادة شهود الفروع الا ان يموت شهود الأصل أو يغيبوا مسيرة ثلاثة ايام فصاعدا او يمرضوا مرضا لا يستطيعون معه حضور مجلس الحكام لان جوازها للحاجة وانما تمس عند عجز الاصل وبهذه الاشياء يتحقق العجز وانما اعتبرنا السفر لان المعجز بعد المسافة ومدة السفر بعيدة حكما حتى ادير عليها عدة من الاحكام فكذا سبيل هذا الحكم وعن ابى يوسف انه كان فى مكان لو غدا لأداء الشهادة لا يستطيع ان يبيت فى اهله صح الاشهاد احياء لحقوق الناس قالوا الاول احسن والثاني اوفق وبه اخذ الفقيه ابو الليث
He said: And the testimony of secondary witnesses is not accepted unless the primary witnesses die, or they are absent for a distance of three days or more, or they become ill with an illness that prevents them from attending the court of judges, because its permissibility is due to necessity, and necessity only arises when the primary is incapacitated, and these things actualize incapacity. And we only consider travel because incapacitation is due to distance, and the duration of travel is considered distant legally, such that many rulings revolve around it. So this ruling follows that. And from Abu Yusuf: If [the primary witness] is in a place such that if he goes in the morning to perform testimony, he cannot return to his family at night, then making a secondary witness is valid to keep alive people's rights. They (the scholars) said: The first saying is better, and the second is more appropriate, and Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted it.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage outlines the conditions for accepting secondary testimony. The default is that primary witnesses must testify directly. Secondary testimony is only allowed when the primary witnesses are truly unable to attend court. The three standard conditions are: (1) death, (2) travel of three days or more, (3) illness preventing attendance. The reason given is necessity (haja). The author also reports a narration from Abu Yusuf who adds a fourth scenario: if the primary witness cannot go to court and return home the same day (i.e., a distance less than three days but still prevents a same-day return). The scholars comment that the first opinion (three conditions) is better (ahsan), but the second (Abu Yusuf's) is more appropriate (awfaq) for the needs of people. Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted Abu Yusuf's view. In practice, the Hanafi school relies on the three conditions as the standard, but the more lenient view is also recognized for necessity.

Key Terms
مسيرة ثلاثة ايام (masirat thalathati ayyam): A journey of three days, considered the distance that justifies secondary testimony.
عجز (‘ajz): Incapacity of the primary witness to attend court, justifying secondary testimony.
حاجة (haja): Necessity that permits secondary testimony as an exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Death of the primary witness
B) Distance of three days or more
C) Temporary minor inconvenience
D) Illness preventing court attendance

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony in Hanafi law is an exception justified by necessity, allowed only when primary witnesses are dead, absent for three days, or ill.

Are Subsidiary Witnesses Agents? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency of subsidiary witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on the agency of subsidiary witnesses and explain the rationale behind each view.

Core Idea
Subsidiary witnesses are not agents, but both views require tahlil for testimony to be authoritative.

In Hanafi fiqh, subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-furu') testify based on the testimony of original witnesses. A key intra-madhhab dispute concerns whether these subsidiary witnesses are agents (wukala') of the original witnesses. This dispute, though it does not affect the practical requirement of tahlil (loading of testimony), reveals important differences in legal reasoning. In this lesson, we will explore the arguments of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, focusing on the counterfactual of revocation to test the agency claim.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Shaykhayn)
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: subsidiary witnesses are NOT agents of original witnesses. Tahlil is still required, but for a different reason: testimony only becomes authoritative (hujjah) when transmitted to the judge's court.
The Shaykhayn deny agency; they use a rational argument based on the inability to revoke.
2
State the opposing view (Imam Muhammad)
Imam Muhammad holds that subsidiary witnesses ARE agents. Therefore, tahlil is necessary to authorize them, just as a principal authorizes an agent in any agency contract.
For Muhammad, revocation by the original witness after tahlil would nullify the subsidiary's authorization.
3
Analyze the counterargument
The text presents a logical test: if the original witness tells the subsidiary to testify and then forbids him, according to the Shaykhayn the forbiddance is invalid and the subsidiary may still testify. If the subsidiary were an agent, forbiddance would end the agency, proving they are not agents. Assess the strength of this argument.
This counterargument is used to refute Muhammad's position.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: although both sides require tahlil, the consequence of revocation differs. For the Shaykhayn, revocation is ineffective; for Muhammad, revocation would nullify the subsidiary's authorization.
The dispute does not change the necessity of tahlil in practice.
5
Note the common ground
Both positions ultimately require tahlil (loading of testimony) for the subsidiary witnesses to be able to testify in court. The difference is purely in the legal characterization (agency vs. non-agency) and the effect of revocation.
This shows that ikhtilaf in reasoning does not always change the final ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہادت نقل کرتا ہے اور وہ اسی وقت وکیل ہوسکتا ہے جب کہ مؤکل اس کو اس کام کا حکم کرے لہذا شاہد فرع بھی اسی وقت وکیل ہو گا جب اس کو شاہد اصل، نقل شہادت کا امر کرے گا اور نقل شہادت کے امر کرنے ہی کا نام تحمیل شہادت ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ محمد کے نزدیک تحمیل شہادت ضروری ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک تحمیل شہادت اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ شیخین کے نزدیک شاہد فرع، شاہد اصل کا وکیل نہیں ہوتا حتی کہ اگر شاہد اصل نے شاہد فرع سے یہ کہا کہ تو میری شہادت پر شہادت دے اور پھر شاہد اصل نے اس کو منع کر دیا تو اس کا منع کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا، اور شاہد فرع کا شاہد اصل کی شہادت پر شہادت دینا جائز ہوگا اگر شاہد فرع، شاہد اصل کا وکیل ہوتا جیسا کہ امام محمد نے کہا ہے تو شاہد اصل کے منع کرنے کے بعد شاہد فرع کو شہادت دینے کا حق نہ ہوتا کیوں کہ مؤکل کے منع کرنے کے بعد وکیل، وکیل نہیں رہتا ہے۔ بہر حال شاہد فرع اگر چہ شاہد اصل کا وکیل نہیں ہے لیکن شہادت اصول کو حجت بنانے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ شہود فرع اصول کی شہادت کو قاضی کی مجلس میں نقل کریں کیوں کہ شہادت فی نفسہ حجت نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس وقت حجت ہوتی ہے جب اس کو قاضی کی مجلس میں منتقل کر دیا جائے بہر حال معلوم ہوا کہ شہود فرع پر شہادت اصول کو حجت بنانے کے لئے مجلس قاضی میں نقل کرنا ضروری ہے اور نقل کرنے کے لئے تحمیل ضروری ہے یعنی شہود فرع، اصول کی شہادت نقل کرنے کے اسی وقت مجاز ہوں گے جبکہ شہود اصل نے ان پر اس شہادت کو لادا ہو اور اس کا ذمہ دار بنایا ہو پس ثابت ہوا کہ تحمیل شہادت شیخین کے نزدیک بھی ضروری ہے۔
He (the witness) transmits testimony and he can only be an agent when the principal orders him to do that work. Therefore, a subsidiary witness will only be an agent when the original witness orders him to transmit the testimony, and ordering to transmit testimony is called tahlil (loading) of testimony. So it is established that according to Muhammad, tahlil is necessary. And according to the Shaykhayn, tahlil is necessary because according to the Shaykhayn, the subsidiary witness is not an agent of the original witness. So much so that if the original witness told the subsidiary witness: 'Bear testimony on my testimony' and then the original witness forbade him, then his forbidding would not be valid, and the subsidiary witness's bearing testimony on the original witness's testimony would be permissible. If the subsidiary witness were an agent of the original witness as Imam Muhammad said, then after the original witness forbade him, the subsidiary witness would not have the right to testify, because after the principal forbids, the agent ceases to be an agent. Nevertheless, although the subsidiary witness is not an agent of the original witness, to make the original testimony authoritative (hujjah), it is necessary that the subsidiary witnesses transmit the original testimony in the judge's court. Because testimony in itself is not authoritative; it becomes authoritative only when it is transmitted to the judge's court. In any case, it is understood that it is necessary for the subsidiary witnesses to transmit the original testimony to the judge's court to make it authoritative, and for transmission, tahlil is necessary. That is, the subsidiary witnesses will only be authorized to transmit the testimony of the originals when the original witnesses have loaded this testimony upon them and made them responsible for it. So it is established that tahlil is also necessary according to the Shaykhayn.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal status of subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-furu') who testify based on the testimony of original witnesses (shuhud al-asl). The key question is whether subsidiary witnesses are agents (wukala') of the original witnesses. Imam Muhammad holds that they are agents, and therefore tahlil (the act of loading the testimony onto them) is required to authorize them. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that they are not agents, yet they still require tahlil for a different reason: because testimony must be transferred to the judge's court to become effective, and that transfer requires authorization. The passage uses a counterfactual argument: if subsidiary witnesses were agents, the original witnesses could revoke their agency by forbidding them, but they cannot, proving they are not agents. Nonetheless, tahlil is necessary in both views. The discussion is from a commentary (likely Ashraf al-Hidayah) explaining the reasoning behind the requirement of tahlil.

Key Terms
شاہد فرع (shāhid farʻ): A subsidiary witness who testifies based on the testimony of an original witness (shāhid aṣl).
تحمیل شہادت (taḥmīl shahādat): The act of the original witness loading the testimony onto the subsidiary witness, i.e., instructing them to bear witness on their behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn, why is tahlil necessary for subsidiary witnesses?
A) Because subsidiary witnesses are agents and need authorization.
B) Because testimony must be transmitted to the judge's court to become authoritative.
C) Because the original witness has the right to revoke.
D) Because subsidiary witnesses must be righteous.

Key Takeaway
Both the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad require tahlil for subsidiary witnesses, but differ on whether the subsidiary is an agent, with the practical difference affecting the effect of revocation.

Shahadat — Testimony

Conditions for Accepting Testimony of Subsidiary Witnesses
Ruling with proof on when subsidiary testimony is accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for accepting subsidiary testimony in the Hanafi school, explain the legal reasoning tying the three-day journey to incapacity, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Subsidiary testimony is a necessity-based concession, accepted only when original witnesses are incapacitated by death, three-day journey, or illness.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on subsidiary testimony — a mechanism to preserve rights when original witnesses cannot testify. You will learn the three conditions for its acceptance, the legal reasoning that ties the three-day journey to incapacity, and the internal differences among the Hanafi imams on the scope of this concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its underlying reason
Start with the base ruling: subsidiary testimony is not accepted unless original witnesses die, are absent for a three-day journey, or are ill. The reason is necessity — subsidiary testimony is a concession for when the original witness is incapacitated.
The base ruling is from al-Quduri, quoted in al-Hidayah.
2
Trace the analogy establishing the three-day journey as standard
The text proves the three-day journey as incapacitating by citing that many rulings (qasr, iftar, dropping Jumu'ah, etc.) are based on this distance. This shows that travel of three days is legally significant and establishes incapacity.
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the illa of distance causing incapacity.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's more flexible position
Abu Yusuf held that subsidiary testimony is accepted if the original witness cannot return home the same day, regardless of the exact distance. This is based on removing hardship and preserving rights.
The text calls this position 'awfaq' (more suitable).
4
Examine Imam Muhammad's unconditional allowance
Imam Muhammad is reported to permit subsidiary testimony in all cases, even if the original witness is in the same mosque. This is the broadest view, prioritizing the preservation of rights over any distance condition.
This view is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah by al-Ayni.
