Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Identification in Shahada 'ala al-Shahada: The Requirement of Additional Witnesses
Explains ruling when secondary witnesses cannot identify the defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on identifying a defendant in shahada 'ala al-shahada and apply the qiyas to property cases.

Core Idea
If secondary witnesses cannot identify the defendant, the claimant must bring two additional witnesses to confirm identity.

In cases of testimony upon testimony, the identity of the defendant must be certain before judgment. This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah where secondary witnesses testify against a known woman by lineage but cannot identify the woman brought to court. The Hanafi school requires two additional witnesses to resolve the uncertainty. Through qiyas, the same principle applies to property disputes, ensuring that the judgment targets the correct person or property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of uncertainty
Recognize the situation: secondary witnesses testified against a woman known by lineage but cannot identify the woman the claimant brought. This creates doubt about the defendant's identity.
The original testimony is valid, but the link to the present person is missing.
2
State the primary ruling for identification of a person
The ruling: the claimant must produce two additional witnesses who testify that the present woman is indeed the one named in the original testimony. Only then can judgment be passed.
This is a procedural requirement, not a new substantive testimony.
3
Understand the illah (legal cause)
The illah is uncertainty about the identity of the object of testimony. The original testimony was against a specific person by lineage, but the present person may not be that same individual.
The illah is jaliyyah (obvious): identity mismatch.
4
Apply the illah to the analogous property case
In the pre-emption (shuf'a) example, the claimant's witnesses testify that a house with specific boundaries was sold, but the buyer denies possession. The illah is the same: uncertainty whether the house in the buyer's possession matches the description. Hence, two additional witnesses are required to confirm possession of that exact property.
The same illah triggers the same remedy.
5
Derive the consistent principle
When testimony is given against a defined entity (person or property), and there is doubt whether the present subject is that entity, the claimant must present additional witnesses to establish identity or possession. This ensures the judgment is executed against the correct person or thing.
This principle upholds justice and avoids potential error.

آخرين يشهدان على ان المحدود بها في يد المدعى عليه وكذا اذا انكر المدعى عليه ان الحدود المذكورة فى الشهادة حدود ما في يديه

ترجمہ اور اگر دو مردوں نے دو مردوں کی گواہی پر فلانہ بنت فلاں فلانیہ پر ایک ہزار درہم کی گواہی دی اور دونوں فرعی گواہوں نے کہا کہ ہم کو اصلی گواہوں نے خبر دی کہ وہ اس عورت کو پہچانتے ہیں پس مدعی ایک عورت کو لایا اور فروع نے کہا کہ ہم نہیں جانتے کہ یہ وہی عورت ہے یا وہ نہیں ہے تو مدعی سے کہا جائے گا کہ تو ایسے دو گواہ لا جو یہ گواہی دیں کہ عورت وہی فلانہ بنت فلانیہ ہے اس لئے کہ نسب پہچانے پر گواہی تو متفق ہو چکی اور مدعی حق کا دعوی کرتا ہے حاضرہ پر ، حالانکہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ اس کے علاوہ ہوں پس اس نسب كو پہچاننا ضروری ہے اور اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ جب گواہ لوگ ایسی محدود چیز کی فروختگی کے گواہ ہوئے جس کے حدود اربعہ ذکر کئے گئے ہیں اور انھوں نے مشتری پر گواہی دی تو دوسرے دو گواہ یہ گواہی دیں کہ جس کے حدود اربعہ ذکر کئے گئے ہیں وہ مدنی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب مدعی علیہ نے اس بات کا انکار کیا کہ جو حدود گواہی میں مذکور ہوئے ہیں وہی حدود اس کے قبضہ میں ہیں۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مشہور فرع نے شہود اصل کی شہادت پر شہادت دی کہ فلانہ بنت فلانہ مثلا زینب بنت حامد قرشی النسل عورت پر فلاں مدعی کا ایک ہزار درہم ہے! اور شہود فرع نے یہ بھی کہا کہ شہود اصل نے ہم کو خبر دی ہے کہ وہ یعنی شہود اصل اس عورت یعنی زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ کو پہچانتے ہیں۔ پھر مدعی ایک عورت کو لایا اور کہا کہ زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ یہ ہے۔ مگر شہود فرع نے کہا کہ ہمیں معلوم نہیں کہ زینب بنت حامد یہی ہے یا یہ نہیں ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں مدعی سے کہا جائے گا کہ زائد ایسے دو گواہ پیش کرو جو اس بات کی شہادت دیں کہ زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ یہی عورت ہے۔

چنانچہ اس گواہی کے بعد ہی اس عورت پر ایک ہزار درہم کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک ہزار درہم کی شہادت ایسی عورت کے خلاف گزر چکی ، جو نسب سے معلوم ہو گئی ۔ یعنی زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ جو نسب کے اعتبار سے معلوم ہے۔ اس پر شہود فرع ایک ہزار درہم کی شہادت دے چکے ہیں لیکن مدعی جس عورت کو پکڑ کر لایا ہے اور اس پر ایک ہزار درہم کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے۔ اس کے بارے میں یہ معلوم نہیں کہ زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ یہی ہے! ہو سکتا ہے زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ نہ ہو بلکہ اس کے علاوہ ہو اور مدعی خواہ مخواہ اس کو پکڑ لایا ہو ۔ اس لئے یہ بات ضروری ہے کہ مدعی ایسے دو گواہ پیش کرے جو اس پر گواہی دیں كه زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ یہی ہے۔ تاکہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ شہادت میں ذکر کردہ نسب اس عورت کا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ متن کے اس مسئلہ کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ خالد نے حامد کو اپنا مکان جس کے حدود اربعہ یہ ہیں فروخت کیا۔ اور حامد مشتری نے اس پر قبضہ بھی کر لیا ہے اور مجھ کو چونکہ حق شفعہ حاصل ہے اسلئے مذکورہ مکان مجھے دلوایا جائے ۔مگر مشتری نے انکار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ میرے قبضہ میں مذکورہ حدود کا کوئی مکان نہیں ہے ۔ تو اس مدعی یعنی شفیع نے دو گواہ پیش کئے ، انھوں نے گواہی دی کہ حامد نے خالد کو فلاں شہر میں ان حدود کے ساتھ ایک مکان خریدا ہے لیکن ہم معین طور پر اس مکان کو نہیں پہچانتے ہیں ۔ تو مدعی یعنی شفیع سے کہا جائے گا کہ دو گواہ اور پیش کرو تا کہ وہ اس بات پر گواہی دیں کہ جو حدود دعوئی اور شہادت میں ذکر کی گئی ہیں۔ اس مدعی علیہ یعنی مشتری کے قبضہ میں انھیں حدود کے ساتھ مکان موجود ہے کیونکہ اس کے بعد ہی قاضی شفیع کے لئے کوئی فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے۔ جس طرح اس مسئلہ میں مزید دو گواہوں کی اس لئے ضرورت ہے کہ وہ اس پر گواہی دیں کہ مشتری کے قبضہ میں وہی مکان موجود ہے جو مکان دعوئی اور شہادت علی الشراء میں مذکور ہے۔ اسی طرح متن کے مسئلہ میں مزید دو گواہ اس بات پر گواہی دیں کہ مدعی جس عورت کو لایا ہے یہ وہی عورت ہے جس کا نسب دعوئی اور شہادت فروع میں بیان کیا گیا تھا اسی طرح اگر ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ فلاں شخص کے قبضہ میں ان حدود کے ساتھ میرا مکان ہے، اس نے ناحق طریقہ سے قبضہ کر رکھا ہے۔ اس مدعی کے گواہوں نے بھی یہی گواہی دی کہ جو حدود دعوئی میں ذکر کی گئی ہیں ان حدود کا مکان مدعی کی ملک ہے اور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ناحق طور پر ہے۔ مگر مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ جو مکان میرے قبضہ میں ہے اس کے حدود اربعہ وہ نہیں ہیں جن کو گواہوں نے ذکر کیا ہے بلکہ اس کے حدود اربعہ اور ہیں۔ غرض یہ کہ جو حدود شہادت میں مذکور ہوئیں مدعی علیہ نے ان حدود کے ساتھ کسی مکان پر اپنے قابض ہونے کا انکار کیا تو مدعی سے کہا جائے گا کہ دو گواہ اور پیش کرو جو اس بات پر گواہی دیں کہ مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں انھیں حدود والا مکان ہے، وہ حدود اربعہ پہلی شہادت میں مذکور ہوئیں۔ یہ مسئلہ بھی متن کے مسئلہ کی نظیر ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح متن کے مسئلہ میں مدعی سے دوسرے دو گواہوں کا مطالبہ کیا گیا تھا اسی طرح یہاں بھی مدعی سے دوسرے دو گواہوں کا مطالبہ کیا گیا ہے۔
Two (witnesses) testify that the defined (property) is in the possession of the defendant, and likewise if the defendant denies that the boundaries mentioned in the testimony are the boundaries of what is in his possession. Translation: And if two men testify on the testimony of two men that So-and-so daughter of So-and-so owes one thousand dirhams, and both secondary witnesses said: 'The primary witnesses informed us that they know that woman.' Then the claimant brought a woman and the secondary witnesses said: 'We do not know if this is that woman or not.' Then the claimant will be told: 'Bring two witnesses who will testify that this woman is indeed that So-and-so daughter of So-and-so.' Because the testimony regarding the lineage is agreed upon, and the claimant claims the right against the present woman, while it is possible that she is someone else. So it is necessary to identify that lineage. And its analogy is: When witnesses testify to the sale of a defined thing whose four boundaries are mentioned, and they testified against the buyer, then two other witnesses should testify that what is defined by those boundaries is in the buyer's possession. And similarly when the defendant denies that the boundaries mentioned in the testimony are the boundaries of what is in his possession. Explanation: The scenario is that the famous secondary witnesses testified on the testimony of the primary witnesses that So-and-so daughter of So-and-so, for example Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya, owes the claimant one thousand dirhams. And the secondary witnesses also said: 'The primary witnesses informed us that they know that woman, i.e., Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya.' Then the claimant brought a woman and said: 'This is Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya.' But the secondary witnesses said: 'We do not know if this is Zaynab bint Hamid or not.' In such a case, the claimant will be told to bring two additional witnesses who will testify that this woman is indeed Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. Then after this testimony, a judgment of one thousand dirhams will be passed against this woman. Because the testimony of one thousand dirhams has been given against a woman who is known by lineage, i.e., Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya known by lineage. The secondary witnesses have already given testimony of one thousand dirhams against her. But the woman the claimant brought and against whom he claims one thousand dirhams is not known to be Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. It is possible that she is not Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya but someone else, and the claimant brought her unnecessarily. Therefore, it is necessary that the claimant produce two witnesses who testify that this is indeed Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya, so that it becomes known that the lineage mentioned in the testimony belongs to this woman. The author of Hidayah said that the analogy (nazir) of this issue is: A person claimed that Khalid sold his house with such-and-such boundaries to Hamid, and Hamid the buyer took possession, and because I have the right of pre-emption (shuf'a), this house should be given to me. But the buyer denied saying: 'There is no house with those boundaries in my possession.' So the claimant (the pre-emptor) produced two witnesses who testified that Hamid bought a house with those boundaries from Khalid in such-and-such city, but we do not specifically know that house. Then the claimant (pre-emptor) will be told to bring two more witnesses to testify that the house with the boundaries mentioned in the claim and testimony is actually in the possession of the defendant (the buyer). Because only then can the judge decide for the pre-emptor. Just as in this issue additional two witnesses are needed to testify that the same house mentioned in the claim and testimony about the purchase is in the buyer's possession, similarly in the original issue, additional two witnesses must testify that the woman brought by the claimant is the same woman whose lineage was stated in the claim and the testimony of the secondary witnesses. Similarly, if a person claims that a certain person has my house with these boundaries and is occupying it wrongfully, and his witnesses testify that the house with those boundaries is owned by the claimant and is wrongfully in the defendant's possession, but the defendant says: 'The house in my possession does not have those boundaries mentioned by the witnesses; its boundaries are different.' In short, the defendant denies possessing any house with the boundaries mentioned in the testimony. Then the claimant will be told to bring two more witnesses to testify that the house with those boundaries is indeed in the defendant's possession. That issue is also an analogy to the original issue. That is, just as in the original issue the claimant was asked for two additional witnesses, here too the claimant is asked for two additional witnesses.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah (Ashraf al-Hidayah) deals with a ruling in shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony). The scenario: Secondary witnesses (shuhud al-far') testify on the basis of primary witnesses that a specific woman (Zaynab bint Hamid) owes 1000 dirhams. However, when the claimant brings a woman, the secondary witnesses cannot confirm that she is that same woman. The ruling: The claimant must bring two additional witnesses who identify the woman as the same one mentioned in the original testimony. The reasoning: The testimony against a specific person (by lineage) is complete, but the identity of the present woman is uncertain. To link the testimony to her, positive identification is required. The author then provides an analogy: In a case of pre-emption (shuf'a) where a house with specific boundaries is claimed, if the buyer denies possession of that exact house, two additional witnesses are needed to confirm that the house with those boundaries is in his possession. Similarly, in a case of wrongful possession where the defendant denies the boundaries, additional witnesses are required to match the boundaries. This illustrates a key principle: When testimony is given against a defined entity (person or property), but there is doubt whether the present subject is that entity, additional proof of identity is necessary. The ruling is clear: additional witnesses for identification are required before judgment can be passed.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony based on the testimony of primary witnesses, i.e., secondary witnesses transmitting the testimony of the original witnesses.
نظير (nazir): Analogy or parallel case used to illustrate the same ruling.
حدود اربعة (hudud arba'a): The four boundaries of a property (east, west, north, south) used to precisely identify real estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are two additional witnesses required in the case of the woman?
A) Because the secondary witnesses are not reliable.
B) To confirm that the woman brought is the same as the one named in the original testimony.
C) Because the primary witnesses were not present.
D) To prove the debt of one thousand dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When there is uncertainty about the identity of the defendant in shahada 'ala al-shahada, the claimant must produce two additional witnesses to resolve that uncertainty before judgment.

The Judge's Letter: A Unique Form of Testimony
Explains that a judge's letter is analogous to shahada 'ala al-shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's letter to another judge and explain why a single letter suffices despite the general requirement of two witnesses.

Core Idea
A single judge's letter carries the weight of two witnesses because of the judge's integrity and authority.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, a written communication from one judge to another (kitab al-qadi) is treated as valid proof, akin to testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada). However, unlike regular secondary witnesses who must be two, a single judge's letter is sufficient. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this exception and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Begin by identifying the main ruling: the judge's letter is analogous to shahada 'ala al-shahada. Note the exception: the writing judge is singled out for transmission.
2
Understand the Exception
Focus on why the exception exists: the judge's perfect integrity (kamil diyanah) and full authority (wafirah wilayah). These qualities make his single testimony reliable, unlike ordinary witnesses.
3
Analyze the Practical Scenario
Work through the scenario: a judge writes to another about a debt owed by Zaynab. When the defendant denies identity, the claimant must bring two witnesses to identify her. This parallels the need for identification in shahada 'ala al-shahada.
This step shows the analogy in action.
4
Examine the Objection and Response
The objection: if the letter is like secondary testimony, why is one judge enough when two witnesses are needed? The Hanafi response (partially given): the judge's unique qualifications make him akin to two witnesses.
The full response, though cut off, centers on the judge's elevated status.
5
Apply the Principle
Conclude that in Hanafi fiqh, a single judge's letter is a valid proof for the receiving judge. Recognize the practical consequence: the receiving judge can act on the letter without additional witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وكذلك كتاب القاضى الى القاضى لانه في معنى الشهادة على الشهادة الا ان القاضى لكمال ديانته ووفور ولايته يتفرد بالنقل

ترجمہ اور اسی طرح کتاب القاضی الی القاضی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ شہادت علی الشہادت کے معنی میں ہے مگر یہ کہ قاضی اپنی کمال دیانت اور تمام ولایت کی وجہ سے اصل کی گواہی نقل کرنے میں متفرد ہے۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ یہی حکم اس وقت ہے جب ایک قاضی نے دوسرے قاضی کو خط لکھا ہو ۔ صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ ایک شہر کے قاضی نے دوسرے شہر کے قاضی کو لکھا کہ دو عادل گواہوں نے میرے سامنے گواہی دی ہے کہ فلاں بن فلاں مدعی کا ایک ہزار درہم زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ پر فی الحال واجب الادا ہے۔ لہذا آپ اس عورت پر یہ حکم صادر فرمائیں جب یہ خط قاضی مکتوب الیہ کو موصول ہوا تو مدعی نے ایک عورت کو حاضر کر کے کہا کہ یہ زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ ہے۔ مگر اس عورت نے زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ ہونے سے انکار کیا تو مدعی سے کہا جائے گا کہ دو گواہ ایسے پیش کرو جو اس پر گواہی دیں کہ یہ عورت وہی زینب بنت حامد قریشیہ ہے، جو قاضی کاتب کے خط میں مذکور ہے تا کہ فیصلہ کرتے وقت قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے لئے اس عورت کی طرف اشارہ کرنا ممکن ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کا تب کا خط شہادت علی الشہادت کے معنی میں ہے۔ گویا اصل گواہوں کی گواہی کو قاضی کا تب نے فرع بن کر قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس پہنچایا ہے۔ اعتراض لیکن اگر یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ قاضی کا تب جب شاہد فرع کے مرتبہ میں ہے تو قاضی کا تب دو شخص ہونے چاہیں کیونکہ شہود فرع کے لئے کم از کم دو ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جواب ... تو اس کا جواب صاحب ہدایہ نے یوں دیا کہ شہود فرع کا بلاشبہ دو ہونا ضروری ہے لیکن قاضی کا تب اپنی دیانت کاملہ اور ولایت
He said: And likewise is the letter of a judge to a judge, because it is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony, except that the judge, due to the completeness of his integrity and abundance of his authority, is singled out for transmission. Translation: And similarly, the letter of a judge to a judge. Because it is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony, except that the judge, due to his perfect integrity and full authority, is unique in transmission. Explanation: The author of Hidayah said that this ruling applies when one judge writes to another judge. The scenario is: A judge of one city wrote to a judge of another city: 'Two just witnesses testified before me that so-and-so son of so-and-so (the claimant) has one thousand dirhams due and payable immediately from Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. Therefore, issue a judgment against this woman.' When this letter reached the addressed judge, the claimant brought a woman and said: 'This is Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya.' But the woman denied being Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. Then the claimant will be told: 'Bring two witnesses who will testify that this woman is indeed that Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya mentioned in the letter of the writing judge, so that at the time of judgment the addressed judge can point to this woman.' The proof is that the letter of the writing judge is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony; as if the writing judge, acting as a secondary witness, conveyed the testimony of the original witnesses to the addressed judge. Objection: But if it is objected that when the writing judge is in the position of a secondary witness, then the writing judge should be two persons, because secondary witnesses must be at least two. Answer: Its answer is given by the author of Hidayah that secondary witnesses indeed must be two, but the writing judge, due to his perfect integrity and authority...
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) to another judge. The ruling: It is akin to shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony), meaning the second judge acts on the letter as if he received testimony from secondary witnesses. However, there is a key difference: the writing judge is unique in that he transmits the original testimony directly, and his integrity and authority make his single testimony sufficient, whereas regular secondary witnesses must be two. The scenario explains: If a judge writes to another judge about a debt owed by a specific woman (Zaynab bint Hamid), and the claimant brings a woman but she denies being that person, the claimant must bring two witnesses to identify her as the person named in the letter. This parallels the earlier ruling on identification in shahada 'ala al-shahada. The objection raised is logical: if the letter is like secondary testimony, why is one judge's letter enough when two witnesses are required? The answer (cut off in the text) is that the judge's office provides the necessary reliability, so a single judge suffices. This is a significant principle in Hanafi judicial procedure: a judge's written communication carries weight equal to two witnesses due to the judge's elevated status.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another containing testimony or a legal decision.
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony of secondary witnesses who attest that they witnessed primary witnesses giving testimony.
كمال ديانت (kamil diyanah): Complete integrity and piety, a quality of a judge that makes his word reliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the claimant can identify the defendant.

Key Takeaway
A single judge's letter is valid proof because the judge's integrity and authority compensate for the usual requirement of two witnesses.

Rule of Additional Witnesses for Property Identity
Explains the requirement of two extra witnesses to verify the property's identity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when additional witnesses are required to confirm property identity and apply it to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Identity of the subject matter requires independent proof; initial witnesses for ownership do not suffice.

This passage expands on a core principle from the matn: when a plaintiff proves ownership but the defendant disputes the identity of the property, the plaintiff must bring two additional witnesses to confirm that the property described is the one in dispute. This ensures that the evidence aligns with the specific object of the claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Recognize the legal situation: plaintiff has already presented witnesses for ownership/primary claim, but defendant denies that the property in his possession matches the description.
This triggers the need for identity proof.
2
Understand the rationale
Ownership and identity are separate facts. The initial witnesses proved ownership, but identity remains unproven. Two additional witnesses are needed to confirm that the defendant's property is the one described.
The number two is derived from general rules of evidence in court.
3
Apply the analogy to the matn's issue
The passage draws an analogy: just as in the matn's issue about a buyer's house and a woman's lineage, two extra witnesses were required, so too in the boundaries dispute two extra witnesses are required.
The analogy is based on the common need for identity verification.
4
Derive the ruling
Conclude that whenever the identity of the subject matter is contested, the plaintiff must produce two additional witnesses specifically to confirm identity.
This is a conditional procedural requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسئلہ میں مزید دو گواہوں کی اس لئے ضرورت ہے کہ وہ اس پر گواہی دیں کہ مشتری کے قبضہ میں وہی مکان موجود ہے جو مکان دعوئی اور شہادت علی الشراء میں مذکور ہے۔ اسی طرح متن کے مسئلہ میں مزید دو گواہ اس بات پر گواہی دیں کہ مدعی جس عورت کو لایا ہے یہ وہی عورت ہے جس کا نسب دعوئی اور شہادت فروع میں بیان کیا گیا تھا اسی طرح اگر ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ فلاں شخص کے قبضہ میں ان حدود کے ساتھ میرا مکان ہے، اس نے ناحق طریقہ سے قبضہ کر رکھا ہے۔ اس مدعی کے گواہوں نے بھی یہی گواہی دی کہ جو حد وداربعہ دعوئی میں ذکر کی گئی ہیں ان حدود کا مکان مدعی کی ملک ہے اور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ناحق طور پر ہے۔ مگر مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ جو مکان میرے قبضہ میں ہے اس کے حدود اربعہ وہ نہیں ہیں جن کو گواہوں نے ذکر کیا ہے بلکہ اس کے حدود اربعہ اور ہیں۔ غرض یہ کہ جو حدود شہادت میں مذکور ہوئیں مدعی اصلیہ نے ان حدود کے ساتھ کسی مکان پر اپنے قابض ہونے کا انکار کیا تو مدعی سے کہا جائے گا کہ حضور دو گواہ اور پیش کرو جو اس بات پر گواہی دیں کہ مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں انھیں حدود والا مکان ہے، : دحدود اربعہ پہلی شہادت میں مذکور ہوئیں۔ یہ مسئلہ بھی متن کے مسئلہ کی نظیر ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح متن کے مسئلہ میں مدعی سے دوسرے دو گواہوں کا مطالبہ کیا گیا تھا اسی طرح یہاں بھی مدعی سے دوسرے دو گواہوں کا مطالبہ کیا گیا ہے۔
In the issue, two additional witnesses are needed because they should testify that the same house that is mentioned in the claim and the testimony on purchase is in the possession of the buyer. Similarly, in the issue of the matn, two additional witnesses should testify that the woman brought by the plaintiff is the same woman whose lineage was mentioned in the claim and the subsidiary testimony. Similarly, if a person claims that my house with these boundaries is in the possession of so-and-so, he has wrongfully taken possession. The plaintiff's witnesses have also testified that the house with the boundaries mentioned in the claim belongs to the plaintiff and is wrongfully in the possession of the defendant. But the defendant said that the house in my possession does not have those boundaries that the witnesses mentioned; rather, its four boundaries are different. In short, the boundaries that were mentioned in the testimony, the defendant denied possessing a house with those boundaries. Then the plaintiff will be told: bring two more witnesses who testify that the house in the defendant's possession is the one with those boundaries. This issue is analogous to the issue of the matn. That is, just as in the matn's issue two additional witnesses were demanded from the plaintiff, similarly here two additional witnesses are demanded from the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling: When a plaintiff brings witnesses to prove ownership of a property, but the defendant claims that the property in his possession is different from the one described, the plaintiff must bring two additional witnesses to confirm the identity of the property. The same applies in cases of lineage or specific items. The ruling is based on the need to establish the identity of the subject matter beyond doubt. This is a continuation of the previous discussion from the matn.

Key Terms
شهادة علي الشراء (shahadat 'ala al-shira'): Testimony on purchase, i.e., witnesses who testify that the plaintiff bought the property.
حدود أربعة (hudud arba'ah): Four boundaries; the legal description of a property by its four sides.
نظير (nadhir): Analogous; the text states that the later issue is analogous to the earlier one.

Judge's Letter to Another Judge as Testimony Upon Testimony
Establishes that a judge's written letter carries the same effect as testimony upon testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a judge's letter to another judge and explain why a single judge suffices despite the analogy to testimony upon testimony.

Core Idea
A judge's written letter is like testimony upon testimony, but one judge suffices due to integrity and authority.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key principle in Hanafi judicial procedure: the letter of a judge to another judge carries the legal weight of testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). However, unlike regular subsidiary testimony which requires two witnesses, a single judge's written communication is sufficient. The text explains the reasoning and addresses a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Analogy
State the ruling: the letter of a judge to another judge is accepted as evidence. Identify the analogy: it is 'in the meaning of testimony upon testimony' (shahada ala al-shahada).
2
Describe the Practical Scenario
Walk through the example: a judge writes about a debt, the plaintiff brings a woman who denies identity. Understand the need for additional witnesses to confirm identity.
This shows how the ruling applies in a real court case.
3
Analyze the Proof (Qiyas)
The proof is analogy (qiyas): the letter transmits testimony just as subsidiary witnesses do. Identify the asl (shahada ala al-shahada), far' (judge's letter), and illa (transmission of testimony).
The Hanafi school uses qiyas jali (clear analogy) here.
4
Examine the Objection and Hanafi Response
The objection: subsidiary testimony requires two witnesses, so why does one judge suffice? The answer: the judge's perfect integrity (diyana) and general authority (wilaya 'amma) make him uniquely qualified, so one is enough.
This distinguishes the judge from ordinary subsidiary witnesses.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He said: Likewise, the book of a judge to another judge, because it is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony, except that the judge, due to his perfect integrity and full authority, is uniquely capable of transmitting the original testimony. Translation: Similarly, the book of a judge to a judge. Because it is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony, except that the judge, due to his perfect integrity and full authority, is uniquely capable of transmitting the original testimony. Explanation: Sahib Quduri said that this ruling applies when one judge writes a letter to another judge. The scenario is: The judge of one city wrote to the judge of another city that two just witnesses have testified before me that the plaintiff, so-and-so, has a debt of one thousand dirhams currently due upon Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. So, you should pass judgment against this woman. When this letter reaches the second judge, the plaintiff brought a woman and said: This is Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. But the woman denied being Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya. Then the plaintiff will be told: Bring two witnesses who testify that this woman is the same Zaynab bint Hamid al-Qurashiyya mentioned in the letter of the first judge, so that the second judge can point to this woman when passing judgment. The evidence is that the letter of the first judge is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony. As if the first judge, acting as a subsidiary witness, transmitted the testimony of the original witnesses to the second judge. Objection: If it is objected that when the first judge is in the position of a subsidiary witness, then there should be two judges, because for subsidiary witnesses, at least two are necessary. Answer: The author of al-Hidayah gave this answer: No doubt two subsidiary witnesses are necessary, but the first judge, due to the perfection of his integrity and general writ [of authority], alone is sufficient in transmitting the testimony of the original witnesses; two are not needed.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that a judge's written correspondence to another judge is legally equivalent to shahada ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony). The proof is that it serves the same function: transmitting testimony from the original witnesses to a second judge who will adjudicate. However, unlike regular subsidiary testimony which requires two witnesses, a single judge suffices because of his high level of integrity (diyana) and his general authority (wilaya 'amma). The text illustrates with an example: if a judge writes about a debt owed by a woman, and the plaintiff brings a woman who denies identity, additional witnesses are needed to confirm the woman's identity. The objection about needing two judges is answered by pointing to the judge's unique qualifications.

Key Terms
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony: when witnesses testify that other witnesses gave testimony before them.
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written judgment or communication from one judge to another, conveying testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It requires two judges
D) It is only accepted if written in the presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judge's written communication is accepted as evidence equivalent to testimony upon testimony, but one judge suffices due to his integrity and authority.

Requirement of Specific Lineage in Testimony: General vs. Specific Nisba
Explains the requirement of specific lineage identification in testimony and judge's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for identification in shahada ala al-shahada and kitab al-qadi, and identify the difference between general and specific lineage attributions.

Core Idea
A general tribe name is too broad; specific clan (fakhdh) is required for valid identification.

In Hanafi testimony law, precise identification of individuals is crucial. This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the level of detail required when identifying a witness or a person in a judge's letter. Simply saying 'she is from Banu Tamim' (al-Tamimiyya) is not enough—you need to name her specific clan (fakhdh). The text also explores an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether mentioning the grandfather suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal contexts
The passage applies to two specific types of legal proceedings: shahada ala al-shahada (witness to a testimony) and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi (a judge's letter to another judge). Determine why precise identification matters in these contexts.
Both involve transmitting information over distances or through intermediaries where direct knowledge of the person is absent.
2
Grasp the ruling on general nisba
The text states that saying 'al-Tamimiyya' is not valid (la yajuz) until the woman is attributed to her fakhdh. Understand the reason: Banu Tamim is a huge tribe; the nisba is too general for certain identification.
The ruling is general: any nisba 'amma (general lineage) is insufficient.
3
Analyze the examples of general vs. specific
The passage gives several examples: Farghaniyya (general) vs. Uzjandi (specific); Samarqandiyya and Bukhariyya (general); attribution to a small lane (specific) vs. large quarter/city (general). Classify each based on the principle of being countable and identifiable.
The key is whether the group is small enough for all members to be individually known.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on grandfather
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, identification can be achieved by mentioning the grandfather (jad). Abu Yusuf opposes this. However, all agree that mentioning the fakhdh suffices because fakhdh is the name of the higher grandfather.
The text resolves: fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather, so the requirement is practically the same.

And if they say in these two chapters 'al-Tamimiyya', it is not valid until they attribute her to her fakhdh (clan), which is the specific tribe. This is because identification is necessary in this and it is not achieved by a general lineage, and it is general with respect to Banu Tamim because they are a people who cannot be counted, and it is achieved by attribution to the fakhdh because it is specific. And it is said: al-Farghaniyya is a general attribution, and al-Uzjandi is a specific attribution. And it is said: al-Samarqandiyya and al-Bukhariyya are general. And it is said: attribution to a small lane is specific, and to a large quarter and city is general. Then, even though identification is completed by mentioning the grandfather according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf according to the apparent narrations, mentioning the fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather because it is the name of the higher grandfather, so it is placed in the position of the lower grandfather. Translation: And if they say in these two forms [shahada ala al-shahada and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi] 'al-Tamimiyya', it is not valid until they attribute the woman to her fakhdh, which is the specific tribe. This invalidity is because identification is necessary in this, and identification is not achieved by a general lineage. 'Al-Tamimiyya' is a general lineage, attributing to Banu Tamim, because they are a people who cannot be counted. And by attributing to the fakhdh, identification is achieved because it is a specific lineage. And it is said: al-Farghaniyya is a general lineage, and al-Uzjandi is a specific lineage. And it is said: al-Samarqandiyya and al-Bukhariyya are general. And it is said: attribution to a small lane is specific, and to a large quarter and city is general. Then, identification, even if it is completed by mentioning the grandfather according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf according to the apparent narrations, but mentioning the fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather because the fakhdh is the name of the higher grandfather, so it is placed in the position of the lower grandfather. Explanation: Allah has divided people into different families and tribes for mutual recognition. Allah says: 'And We have made you into peoples and tribes that you may know one another.' There are six types of tribes: Sha'b, Qabila, Fasila, 'Imara, Batn, Fakhdh. The most general is in Sha'b, then gradually specificity increases until Fakhdh is the most specific. So it is said that Sha'b encompasses Qaba'il, Qabila encompasses Fasā'il, Fasila encompasses 'Amā'ir, 'Imara encompasses Butūn, and Batn encompasses Afkhādh. Some have said that Fasila comes after Fakhdh, meaning that according to them the most specific is in Fasila. According to this view, Khuzayma is a Sha'b, Kinana is a Qabila, Quraysh is an 'Imara, Qusayy is a Batn, ...
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of proper identification (ta'rīf) in two types of testimony: shahada ala al-shahada and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi. It states that a general lineage attribution (nisba 'āmma) like 'al-Tamimiyya' (from Banu Tamim) is insufficient because Banu Tamim is a large tribe. Instead, the woman must be attributed to her specific clan (fakhdh), which is a smaller subdivision that allows for precise identification. The text then gives examples of general vs. specific attributions in various regions (e.g., Farghaniyya general vs. Uzjandi specific; Samarqandiyya and Bukhariyya general; attribution to a small lane specific, etc.). Then it mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, identification can also be achieved by mentioning the grandfather (jad), but according to Abu Yusuf (in the apparent narrations), mentioning the grandfather is not sufficient? Actually the text states: 'identification is completed by mentioning the grandfather according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf on the apparent narrations.' This means that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad accept the grandfather as sufficient for identification, while Abu Yusuf apparently does not. However, the text then says that mentioning the fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather because the fakhdh is the name of the higher grandfather, so it is considered like the lower grandfather. The commentary further explains the hierarchy of tribal subdivisions: Sha'b (nation), Qabila (tribe), Fasila (clan), 'Imara (sub-clan), Batn (family), Fakhdh (clan subgroup). There is a difference of opinion on the order, with some placing Fasila after Fakhdh.

Key Terms
فخذ (fakhdh): A clan or subtribe; a specific division of a tribe that allows for precise identification.
نسبت عامہ (nisba 'amma): A general lineage attribution, such as 'Tamimi', which is too broad for precise identification.
نسبت خاصہ (nisba khassa): A specific lineage attribution, such as attribution to a particular clan (fakhdh) or small lane.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A general tribe name (nisba 'amma) is legally insufficient for identification in testimony and judge's letters; a specific fakhdh (clan) is required, which also serves as a substitute for the grandfather in case of dispute.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Requirement of Specific Lineage (Fakhdh) in Testimony Upon Testimony
Ruling with proof: explains that identification requires specific tribal attribution in shahadah 'ala al-shahadah and kitab al-qadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why mentioning the sub-tribe (fakhdh) is required in shahadah 'ala al-shahadah and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi, and state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sufficiency of mentioning the grandfather.

Core Idea
In special testimonies, general attribution is insufficient; the fakhdh or equivalent specificity is needed for valid identification.

This passage from the Kitab al-Shahadah addresses a crucial detail: how precisely must a witness identify a person in secondary testimony or a judge's letter? The Hanafi school, known for its meticulousness, requires a level of specificity that prevents any ambiguity. We will examine why 'al-Tamimiyyah' is not enough and learn about the tribal hierarchy that structures this requirement, as well as a nuanced difference of opinion between the founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Special Contexts
Recognize that the ruling applies to shahadah 'ala al-shahadah (testimony upon testimony) and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi (a judge's letter to another judge). These are cases where precise identification is most critical because the original witness is not present.
These are distinct from ordinary testimony in court.
2
Distinguish General vs. Specific Attribution
Understand the difference between nisbah 'ammah (general attribution) and nisbah khassah (specific attribution). A general attribution (e.g., 'Tamimiyyah') refers to a large group that cannot uniquely identify a person, while a specific attribution (e.g., naming the fakhdh or a small alley) narrows it down sufficiently.
The text gives examples: 'Farghaniyyah' is general, 'Uzjandiyyah' is specific; 'Samarqandiyyah' and 'Bukhariyyah' are general; a small alley is specific, a large neighborhood or city is general.
3
Apply the Rule to the Case of 'Tamimiyyah'
If a witness only says 'al-Tamimiyyah' (attributing the woman to the tribe of Tamim), the testimony is not valid until the specific sub-tribe (fakhdh) is mentioned. The reasoning is that Banu Tamim is a vast tribe with countless individuals, so the attribution is too vague.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Grandfather
According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani, identification can also be achieved by mentioning the grandfather (al-jadd). Abu Yusuf, on the apparent narrations, disagrees and insists on the fakhdh. However, the text states that mentioning the fakhdh is equivalent to mentioning the highest grandfather, so it suffices for all.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that the grandfather suffices, but specifically naming the fakhdh is better and also suffices.

If they said in these two chapters [shahadah 'ala al-shahadah and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi] 'al-Tamimiyyah' (attributing the woman to the tribe of Tamim), it is not permissible until they attribute her to her fakhdh (sub-tribe), which is the specific tribe. This is because identification is necessary in this matter, and it is not achieved by a general attribution, and 'Tamimiyyah' is a general attribution relative to Banu Tamim because they are a people who cannot be counted; but it is achieved by attribution to the fakhdh because it is specific. And it is said: 'al-Farghaniyyah' is a general attribution and 'al-Uzjandiyyah' is specific. And it is said: 'al-Samarqandiyyah' and 'al-Bukhariyyah' are general. And it is said: attribution to a small alley is specific, while attribution to a large neighborhood or city is general. Moreover, although identification is achieved by mentioning the grandfather according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf according to the apparent narrations, mentioning the fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather because it is the name of the highest grandfather, so it is placed in the status of the lower grandfather. Translation: And if in these two situations – shahadah 'ala al-shahadah and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi – they said 'Tamimiyyah', it is not permissible until they attribute this woman to her fakhdh, which is the specific tribe. This impermissibility is because identification is necessary, and identification is not obtained by a general attribution. And 'Tamimiyyah' is a general attribution, attributing to Banu Tamim, because they are a people who cannot be counted. But identification is obtained by attributing to the fakhdh because it is a specific attribution. And it is said that 'Farghaniyyah' is a general attribution and 'Uzjandiyyah' is specific. And it is said that 'Samarqandiyyah' and 'Bukhariyyah' are general. And it is said that attributing to a small alley is specific, and to a large neighborhood or city is general. Then, according to Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad, contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf on the apparent narrations, although identification is completed by mentioning the grandfather, mentioning the fakhdh stands in place of the grandfather because the fakhdh is the name of the higher grandfather, so it is reduced to the level of the lower grandfather. Explanation: For the purpose of mutual acquaintance and distinction among people, Allah the Exalted has divided people into different families and tribes. As the Exalted says: 'And We have made you into nations and tribes so that you may know one another.' There are six tribes: Sha'b, Qabilah, Fasilah, 'Imarah, Batn, Fakhdh. The greatest generality is in Sha'b, then according to order generality decreases. Thus in Fakhdh there is the greatest specificity. For this reason it is said that Sha'b encompasses tribes, Qabilah encompasses Fasilah, Fasilah encompasses 'Imarah, 'Imarah encompasses Batn, and Batn encompasses Fakhdh. Some scholars said that Fasilah comes after Fakhdh, as if according to them the greatest specificity is in Fasilah. According to this saying, Khuzaymah is a Sha'b, Kinanah is a Qabilah, Quraysh is an 'Imarah, Qusayy is a Batn.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Shahadah deals with the requirement of precise identification in two special types of testimony: shahadah 'ala al-shahadah (testimony upon testimony) and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi (a judge's letter to another judge). In these cases, the witnesses must identify the person in question with sufficient specificity. The ruling states that simply attributing someone to a large, well-known tribe like Banu Tamim is insufficient because the tribe is too large for unique identification. Instead, the witness must specify the sub-tribe (fakhdh) such as a smaller clan within Banu Tamim. The author then discusses various examples: attributing to a city like Samarqand is general, while attributing to a specific small alley or sub-tribe is specific. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani, identification can be achieved by mentioning the grandfather (al-jadd), but according to Abu Yusuf (on the apparent narrations), it is not enough. However, the fakhdh takes the place of the grandfather because it is like the highest ancestor. The commentary then explains the six levels of tribal divisions (Sha'b, Qabilah, Fasilah, 'Imarah, Batn, Fakhdh) based on the Quranic verse 49:13, showing that the most specific is Fakhdh (or according to some, Fasilah). This demonstrates the meticulous approach of Hanafi fiqh in ensuring legal testimony is unambiguous and reliable.

Key Terms
الفخذ (al-fakhdh): The sub-tribe or clan, the smallest unit of tribal division in the hierarchy, used for precise identification.
النسبة العامة (al-nisbah al-ammah): A general attribution, such as to a large tribe or city, which does not uniquely identify a person.
النسبة الخاصة (al-nisbah al-khassah): A specific attribution, such as to a sub-tribe or small alley, which uniquely identifies a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In shahadah 'ala al-shahadah, if a witness says 'I testify that al-Tamimiyyah owes 1000 dirhams,' what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted because Tamim is a known tribe.
B) The testimony is not accepted until the witness specifies her sub-tribe (fakhdh).
C) The testimony is accepted only if the witness also mentions her father's name.
D) The testimony is rejected entirely because women's testimony is not accepted in debt cases.

Key Takeaway
In shahadah 'ala al-shahadah and kitab al-qadi, the witness must identify the person with a specific sub-tribe (fakhdh) or an equivalent specific attribution; general tribal/city affiliation is insufficient.

Shahadat — Testimony

Punishment for False Witness: Tashhir vs. Ta'zir
Dispute on false witness punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-school dispute on false witness punishment and explain the proofs for each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says only public disgrace; the Sahibayn say disgrace plus lashes—and their proof from Umar's practice carries weight.

False testimony is a grave offense. But what punishment does a false witness deserve? Imam Abu Hanifa argued that public humiliation alone suffices, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, held that physical punishment is also required. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa (only tashhir) and the Sahibayn (tashhir + ta'zir + imprisonment). Note that the majority of scholars (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree with the Sahibayn.
The Sahibayn's view is also the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Identify the dalil: the narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab that he gave forty lashes and blackened the face of a false witness, and his written instruction to his governors in Syria.
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted proof) from the action of a Companion.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection states that the narration includes blackening the face (which the Sahibayn do not require) and forty lashes (exceeding the ta'zir maximum of 39). How do you respond?
The point is to establish the principle of ta'zir, not every detail.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response is that Umar's action is cited to negate Abu Hanifa's view that no ta'zir is given. The narration proves that striking (darb) is legislated for false testimony, regardless of the specific number or additional rituals.
This shows how Hanafi usul handles objections by focusing on the core legal principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, only tashhir; under the Sahibayn, tashhir + ta'zir + imprisonment. Know which view is operative for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, as supported by the majority and later Hanafi authorities.

اس اثر سے بھی جھوٹے گواہ کی تعزیر ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور حضرت عمر جیسے جلیل القدر الو العزم صحابی کی تقلید ہمارے لئے حجت ہے۔ اعتراض اس استدلال پر یہ اعتراض کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ حضرت عمرؓ کے اس اثر میں منہ کالا کر۔ كما ذكر ہے۔ حالانکہ صاحبین اس کے ز کے قائل نہیں ہیں اور تعزیر میں کوڑوں کی تعداد چالیس کو نہیں پہنچتی ہے یعنی تعزیر میں زیادہ سے زیادہ انتالیس کوڑے مارے جا سکتے ہیں ۔ حالانکہ اس اثر میں چالیس کوڑوں کا ذکر ہے۔
جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر کے اثر سے مقصود امام صاحب کے قول کی نفی کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب تعزیر کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ بہر حال یہ اثر اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ جھوٹی گواہی کی تعزیر میں نفس ضرب ( مارنا) ثابت ہے۔
False testimony is mentioned in a separate chapter because it has specific rulings, and it is mentioned at the end because the original [subject] is true testimony. False testimony is when a witness admits that he gave false testimony, or for example a person testified that Khalid was killed, then he sees that Khalid is alive – this testimony would also be false. In short, either the witness himself admits, or it becomes known with certainty through some external evidence that he is false. In any case, Imam Abu Hanifah said: 'I will publicly disgrace the false witness in the market and humiliate him, and I will not give him ta'zir, i.e., I will not whip him.' The Sahibayn said: 'He will be whipped and also imprisoned.' This is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and the majority of scholars. The proof of the Sahibayn is the narration from Umar al-Faruq that he gave forty lashes to a false witness and blackened his face. This narration indicates the legislation of ta'zir. Also, from Walid ibn Abi Malik [it is narrated] that Umar wrote to his governors in Syria: 'The false witness should be given forty lashes, his face blackened, his head shaved, and his imprisonment prolonged.' This narration also proves ta'zir for the false witness. And following the example of a great and resolute companion like Umar is a proof for us. Objection: It can be objected that in this narration of Umar, blackening the face is mentioned, whereas the Sahibayn do not hold it, and the number of lashes in ta'zir does not reach forty – i.e., in ta'zir the maximum is thirty-nine lashes – while this narration mentions forty. Response: The answer is that the purpose of the narration from Umar is to negate the saying of Imam [Abu Hanifah], because Imam [Abu Hanifah] does not hold ta'zir. In any case, this narration indicates that in the ta'zir of false testimony, striking (whipping) itself is established.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from the 'Kitab al-Shahadah' discusses the punishment for false testimony (shahadat al-zur). It begins by defining false testimony: either the witness confesses to lying, or external evidence conclusively proves the testimony false (e.g., testifying someone was killed when the person is alive). Then it presents the dispute. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the false witness should only be publicly disgraced (tashhir) in the market, without physical punishment (ta'zir). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that he should also receive ta'zir (discretionary lashes) and imprisonment. The text notes that this is also the position of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and the majority of scholars. The Sahibayn's proof is a narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab that he gave forty lashes to a false witness and blackened his face, as well as a written instruction from Umar to his governors. The commentary then raises an objection: the narration includes blackening the face and forty lashes, but the Sahibayn themselves do not require blackening the face, and forty lashes exceeds the maximum for ta'zir (which is thirty-nine according to Hanafi law). The response is that the point of citing Umar's action is to refute Abu Hanifah's view that no ta'zir is given at all, not to adopt every detail. Thus the narration proves the principle of physical punishment (darb) for false witnesses. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of weighing proofs from the actions of the Companions and addressing objections.

Key Terms
شاهد الزور (shahid al-zur): A false witness, one who gives false testimony knowingly.
التشهير (al-tashhir): Public disgrace, such as parading the witness in the market and announcing his crime.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes without fixed hadd, such as lashes or imprisonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what punishment does a false witness receive?
A) Only public disgrace (tashhir)
B) Only ta'zir (lashes)
C) Ta'zir, tashhir, and imprisonment
D) Death penalty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that a false witness receives public disgrace (tashhir), discretionary lashes (ta'zir), and imprisonment, based on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Punishment of False Witness: Tashhir vs. Ta'zir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on punishment of false witness with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the punishment of a false witness, explain the proofs each side uses, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For a false witness, Abu Hanifa only exposes; the Sahibayn also beat and imprison.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on how to punish a false witness (shahid al-zur). Imam Abu Hanifa maintains that public exposure (tashhir) suffices as a deterrent, while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), insist on discretionary beating (ta'zir) and imprisonment. The disagreement turns on the interpretation of practices of the early community, especially the actions of Caliph Umar and the qadi Shuraih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
State clearly what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn prescribe for punishing a false witness.
Abu Hanifa: tashhir only. Sahibayn: ta'zir (beating) and imprisonment, and also tashhir.
2
Extract the proof of each side
Sahibayn rely on the action of Umar (40 lashes and face blackening). Abu Hanifa relies on the practice of Shuraih and a deterrent-based reasoning.
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response to the Sahibayn's proof
Abu Hanifa argues Umar's action was a matter of policy (siyasah), not a fixed legal punishment.
Indicators: specific number 40 and face blackening.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: a judge following Abu Hanifa would only expose; following Sahibayn would also beat and imprison.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and why
The Sahibayn's view is preferred because it aligns with the majority of scholars (al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad).
Al-Sarakhsi notes tashhir is also done according to them.

فصل قال ابو حنيفة شاهد الزور أشهرة في السوق ولا اعزره وقالا نوجعه ضربا ونحيسه وهو قول الشافعى لهما ما روى عن عمر رضى الله عنه انه ضرب شاهد الزور اربعين سوطا وسخم وجهه ولان هذه كبيرة يتعدى ضررها الى العباد وليس فيها حدّ مقرّر فيُعزّر وله ان شريحا كان يُشهره ولا يضرب ولان الانزجار يحصل بالتشهير فيكتفى به والضرب وان كان مبالغة فى الزجر ولكنه يقع مانعا عن الرجوع فوجب التخفيف نظرا الى هذا الوجه وحديث عمر رضى الله عنه محمول على السياسة بدلالة التبليغ الى الاربعين والتسخيم ثم تفسير التشهير منقول عن شريح فانه كان يبعثه الى سوقه ان كان سوقيا والى قومه ان كان غير سوقى بعد العصر اجمع ما كانوا ويقولون ان شريحا يقرأ عليكم السلام ويقول انا وجدنا هذا شاهد زور فاحذروه وحذروا الناس منه وذكر شمس الائمة السرخسى انه يُشهر عندهما ايضا والتعزير والحبس على قدر ما يراه القاضى عندهما وكيفية التعزيز ما ذكرناه في الحدود
Section: Abu Hanifa said: I will expose the false witness in the market and not punish him (ta'zir). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: We will inflict beating and imprison him. And it is the statement of al-Shafi'i. Their proof is what was narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he beat a false witness forty lashes and blackened his face. And because this is a great sin whose harm extends to the servants of Allah, and there is no fixed punishment for it, so ta'zir is prescribed. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that Shuraih used to expose him and not beat him. And because deterrence is achieved by exposure, so it suffices. Beating, although excessive in deterrence, becomes a barrier to retraction, so leniency is obligatory considering this aspect. And the hadith of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) is interpreted as a policy measure, as indicated by reaching forty (lashes) and blackening the face. Then the explanation of exposure is transmitted from Shuraih: he would send him to his market if he was a market person, and to his people if he was not a market person, after Asr when they are most gathered, and they would say: 'Shuraih sends you greetings and says: We found this one to be a false witness, so beware of him and warn others about him.' And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that he is also exposed according to them (the two), and ta'zir and imprisonment are according to what the judge deems appropriate according to them. And the manner of ta'zir is what we mentioned in the Book of Hudud.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the punishment of a false witness (shahid al-zur). The text presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), along with their respective proofs. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the false witness should only be publicly exposed (tashhir) and not subjected to discretionary beating (ta'zir). His proof is the practice of the qadi Shuraih, who would expose false witnesses but not beat them, and the reasoning that exposure alone suffices for deterrence, while beating may prevent the witness from retracting his false testimony. The Sahibayn, agreeing with Imam al-Shafi'i and others, hold that the false witness should be beaten and imprisoned, based on the practice of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab, who beat a false witness forty lashes and blackened his face. They argue that false testimony is a major sin (kabirah) that harms others and has no fixed hadd, thus requiring ta'zir. The text then reconciles Umar's action as a matter of state policy (siyasah), not a fixed legal punishment. It also notes that according to al-Sarakhsi, the Sahibayn also accept tashhir in addition to ta'zir. The judge's discretion determines the severity of ta'zir and imprisonment. This passage illustrates the Hanafi school's nuanced approach: while the Sahibayn's view may be more commonly adopted, the school preserves the ikhtilaf, and the judge considers the circumstances.

Key Terms
شاهد زور (shahid al-zur): A witness who gives false testimony in court.
تشهير (tashhir): Public exposure of the false witness, making him known as a liar.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for sins with no fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the prescribed punishment for a false witness?
A) Only public exposure (tashhir)
B) Beating and imprisonment, along with exposure
C) Execution
D) Fining

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains an internal dispute on punishing false witnesses: Abu Hanifa opts for exposure alone, while the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment, and the latter view prevails.

Shahadat — Testimony

The Legal Definition of Fakhdh and Its Role in Testimony Identification
Definition of fakhdh and ruling on necessary specificity in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fakhdh and explain why general attribution (nisbat 'ammah) invalidates testimony.

Core Idea
A person cannot be identified by a general tribe name; the specific clan (fakhdh) is necessary for valid testimony.

Testimony requires precise identification of the witness or debtor. The Hanafi school has established that a general tribal name like 'Tamimiyya' is insufficient because it can refer to countless individuals. This lesson introduces the concept of fakhdh, the specific sub-tribe, and how it fulfills the need for unique identification in legal documents.

Guided Path
1
Define fakhdh per al-Quduri
Read the definition: fakhdh is the specific tribe after which there is no smaller family unit. Example: Hashim is a fakhdh of Quraysh, and Abbas is a fasila (family) of Hashim.
This definition comes from the commentary on al-Quduri.
2
Identify the ruling scenario
The passage discusses shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony on testimony) and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi (letter of a judge). In these contexts, when a debtor is mentioned, her identification must be specific.
The scenario: a woman debtor named Zaynab bint Hamid al-Tamimiyyah.
3
Understand the illah (reason)
The reason is that the relationship (nisbat) must allow for identification (ma'rifah). General attribution does not achieve this because many people share the same larger tribe.
The phrase 'عام نسبت سے شناخت حاصل نہیں ہوتی' is key.
4
Distinguish general vs specific attribution
Attribution to a large region (e.g., Ferghana) is general; attribution to a specific city (e.g., Uzgand) may be specific but can become general if the city is large. Similar for neighborhoods and alleys in cities like Samarkand.
The passage gives examples from the author's time; today similar principles apply.
5
Apply to the Zaynab example
Zaynab bint Hamid al-Tamimiyyah is invalid because Banu Tamim has countless women. If she is attributed to her fakhdh (e.g., al-Hashimiyyah if her clan is Hashim), it becomes valid.
The ruling: 'جائز نہیں' for general, 'جائز ہے' for specific.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے، ہاشم مفخذ ہے، عباس فصیلہ" ہے۔ یہاں قدوری میں فخذ سے مراد وہ قبیلہ خاصہ ہے جس کے بعد کوئی خاصہ کنبہ نہ ہو۔ اس تمہید کے بعد ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ شہادت علی الشہادت اور کتاب القاضی الی القاضی میں قرضدار عورت کی نسبت بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ زینب بنت حامد تمیمیہ پر فلاں بن فلاں کے ایک ہزار درہم قرض ہیں تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ ہاں اگر اس عورت کو اس کے قبیلہ خاصہ کی طرف منسوب کیا یعنی اس کے خاصہ کنبہ کی طرف منسوب کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نسبت ایسی ہونی چاہئے جس میں آدمی کی شناخت ہو سکے۔ اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ آدمی کی شناخت عام نسبت سے حاصل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے تمیمہ اور تمیمہ عام نسبت ہے جو بنو تمیم کی طرف منسوب ہے کیونکہ بنو تمیم کے بے شمار افراد ہیں پس اس قوم میں نہ جانے کتنی عورتیں ایسی ہوں گی ۔ جن کے نام مع ان کے باپ متفق ہیں ۔ لہذا صرف تمیمہ کہنے سے کسی عورت کی شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی ہے ۔ ہاں اگر عورت کو اس کے فخذ یعنی خاص قبیلہ کی طرف منسوب کیا تو چونکہ یہ نسبت خاصہ ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے شناخت حاصل ہو جائے گی ۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ صوبہ فرغائنہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے اور اس صوبہ کے ایک شہر اوز جند کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے لیکن یہ بہت پہلے کی بات ہے ور نہ آجکل اور اوز جند خود بڑا شہر ہے۔ اور جند کی طرف نسبت سے بھی پوری شناخت حاصل ہونے میں تامل ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ سمرقند یا بخارا کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے اور ان کے کسی محلہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ چھوٹے کوچہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے اور بڑے محلہ اور شہر کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کسی کا تعارف کراتے ہوئے باپ کا ذکر کافی ہے۔ دادا کے ذکر کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طرفین کے نزدیک دادا کا ذکر کرنا بھی ضروری ہے لیکن فخذ یعنی خاص کنبہ کا ذکر بھی دادا کے ذکر کے قائم مقام ہے کیونکہ فخذ بھی جد اعلیٰ کے نام پر ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس کو جداد نی (دادا) کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا۔
Hashim is a fakhdh (sub-tribe), Abbas is a fasila (family). Here in al-Quduri, by fakhdh is meant the specific tribe after which there is no specific family. After this introduction, observe that in testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) and the letter of a judge to another judge (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi), when mentioning a woman debtor, it is said: 'Zaynab bint Hamid al-Tamimiyyah owes so-and-so one thousand dirhams.' This is not permissible. Yes, if the woman is attributed to her specific sub-tribe (fakhdh), i.e., her specific family, then it is permissible. The reason is that the relationship must be such that the person can be identified. It is also agreed that identification is not achieved through a general relationship, like Tamim and Tamimiyya, which is a general relationship attributed to Banu Tamim, because Banu Tamim has countless individuals. So many women of that tribe have names and fathers that coincide. Therefore, just saying Tamimiyya does not identify a woman. Yes, if the woman is attributed to her fakhdh, i.e., specific tribe, then because this relationship is specific, identification will be achieved. Some scholars said that attribution to the province of Ferghana is general attribution, and attribution to the city of Uzgand in that province is specific attribution, but this is from a long time ago; nowadays Uzgand itself is a big city, and identification by attribution to Uzgand is also uncertain. Some scholars said that attribution to Samarkand or Bukhara is general, and attribution to a specific neighborhood (mahalla) is specific. Some said that attribution to a small alley (kocha) is specific, and to a big neighborhood or city is general. The author of al-Hidayah said that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, when introducing someone, mentioning the father is sufficient; there is no need to mention the grandfather. And according to the two (those of both sides), mentioning the grandfather is also necessary. But mentioning the fakhdh (specific clan) stands in place of mentioning the grandfather, because fakhdh is also named after a great ancestor. So it is brought down to the level of the grandfather.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'fakhdh' (specific sub-tribe) and explains its legal significance in testimony, specifically in shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony on testimony) and kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi (letter of a judge to another judge). The ruling is that to validly identify a witness or a debtor in such contexts, a general tribe name (like Tamim) is insufficient because it may refer to many individuals. Instead, one must use the fakhdh, i.e., the specific clan or sub-tribe after which there is no smaller family unit. The passage provides examples: Hashim is a fakhdh of Quraysh, Abbas is a fasila (family) of Hashim. The underlying reason (illah) is that the identification (ma'rifah) of the person must be achievable. The text then discusses practical applications: attribution to a large region (like Ferghana) is general, while to a specific city (like Uzgand) may be specific but can become general if the city is large. Similarly, for cities like Samarkand and Bukhara, a neighborhood or alley is specific. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that mentioning the father suffices for identification, whereas 'the two' (possibly Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require mention of the grandfather, though fakhdh can substitute for grandfather. This shows the Hanafi school's attention to legal precision in procedural matters.

Key Terms
فخذ (fakhdh): The specific sub-tribe or clan that is directly above the family (fasila), such that there is no smaller named group.
فصیلہ (fasila): The family unit, smaller than a fakhdh, e.g., Banu Abbas is a fasila of Banu Hashim.
نسبت عامہ (nisbat 'ammah): General attribution, e.g., to a large tribe or region, insufficient for identification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to identify a woman debtor as 'Zaynab bint Hamid al-Tamimiyyah' in a letter of a judge?
A) Because she is not from Banu Tamim
B) Because the name 'Tamimiyyah' is too general and does not uniquely identify her
C) Because women cannot be debtors in Hanafi law
D) Because the father's name is missing

Key Takeaway
For testimony to be valid, the identification must be specific to the level of fakhdh; general tribe names do not suffice.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Father vs Grandfather in Identification and the Role of Fakhdh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage specificity in identification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding the necessity of mentioning the grandfather in testimony identification and explain how fakhdh can substitute for the grandfather.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf suffices with father; the two require grandfather; but fakhdh can stand in for grandfather as it is named after an ancestor.

While the Hanafi school agrees that specific identification is necessary, there is an internal dispute on the level of lineage required. This lesson examines the views of Imam Abu Yusuf and the two (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) on whether mentioning the father alone is enough or if the grandfather must be added. It also explains the innovative ruling that mentioning the fakhdh (specific clan) can replace the grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Recall the requirement for specific identification
From the previous lesson, we know that general attribution is invalid. The question now is: how specific must the lineage be? The father's name is already included in the standard identification (e.g., 'Zaynab bint Hamid'). Is that sufficient?
The dispute arises after the fakhdh requirement is settled.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that mentioning the father alone is sufficient. There is no need to mention the grandfather. His reasoning is likely based on custom: in many cases, the father's name is enough to distinguish the person within the specific clan.
His view is attributed to him in al-Hidayah.
3
State the position of 'the two' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
The two hold that the grandfather must also be mentioned for complete identification. However, they acknowledge that if the fakhdh is mentioned, it suffices in place of the grandfather.
The phrase 'طرفین' likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
4
Explain the substitution of fakhdh for grandfather
The reason given is that the fakhdh is also named after a great ancestor (e.g., Banu Hashim is named after Hashim, a great-grandfather of the Prophet). Therefore, mentioning the fakhdh is equivalent to mentioning the grandfather or even higher ancestor.
This is a practical solution that resolves the dispute.
5
Determine the practical application
In practice, when identifying a person, one can either mention the father (per Abu Yusuf) or include the grandfather (per the two). But to be safe and avoid the dispute, one can simply mention the fakhdh, which covers both requirements.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated, but the use of fakhdh is the recommended approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے، ہاشم مفخذ ہے، عباس فصیلہ" ہے۔ یہاں قدوری میں فخذ سے مراد وہ قبیلہ خاصہ ہے جس کے بعد کوئی خاصہ کنبہ نہ ہو۔ اس تمہید کے بعد ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ شہادت علی الشہادت اور کتاب القاضی الی القاضی میں قرضدار عورت کی نسبت بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ زینب بنت حامد تمیمیہ پر فلاں بن فلاں کے ایک ہزار درہم قرض ہیں تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ ہاں اگر اس عورت کو اس کے قبیلہ خاصہ کی طرف منسوب کیا یعنی اس کے خاصہ کنبہ کی طرف منسوب کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نسبت ایسی ہونی چاہئے جس میں آدمی کی شناخت ہو سکے۔ اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ آدمی کی شناخت عام نسبت سے حاصل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے تمیمہ اور تمیمہ عام نسبت ہے جو بنو تمیم کی طرف منسوب ہے کیونکہ بنو تمیم کے بے شمار افراد ہیں پس اس قوم میں نہ جانے کتنی عورتیں ایسی ہوں گی ۔ جن کے نام مع ان کے باپ متفق ہیں ۔ لہذا صرف تمیمہ کہنے سے کسی عورت کی شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی ہے ۔ ہاں اگر عورت کو اس کے فخذ یعنی خاص قبیلہ کی طرف منسوب کیا تو چونکہ یہ نسبت خاصہ ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے شناخت حاصل ہو جائے گی ۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ صوبہ فرغائنہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے اور اس صوبہ کے ایک شہر اوز جند کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے لیکن یہ بہت پہلے کی بات ہے ور نہ آجکل اور اوز جند خود بڑا شہر ہے۔ اور جند کی طرف نسبت سے بھی پوری شناخت حاصل ہونے میں تامل ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ سمرقند یا بخارا کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے اور ان کے کسی محلہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ چھوٹے کوچہ کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت خاصہ ہے اور بڑے محلہ اور شہر کی طرف نسبت کرنا نسبت عامہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کسی کا تعارف کراتے ہوئے باپ کا ذکر کافی ہے۔ دادا کے ذکر کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طرفین کے نزدیک دادا کا ذکر کرنا بھی ضروری ہے لیکن فخذ یعنی خاص کنبہ کا ذکر بھی دادا کے ذکر کے قائم مقام ہے کیونکہ فخذ بھی جد اعلیٰ کے نام پر ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس کو جداد نی (دادا) کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا۔

Commentary

The ruling is that to validly identify a witness or a debtor in such contexts, a general tribe name (like Tamim) is insufficient because it may refer to many individuals. Instead, one must use the fakhdh, i.e., the specific clan or sub-tribe after which there is no smaller family unit. The passage provides examples: Hashim is a fakhdh of Quraysh, Abbas is a fasila (family) of Hashim. The underlying reason (illah) is that the identification (ma'rifah) of the person must be achievable. The text then discusses practical applications: attribution to a large region (like Ferghana) is general, while to a specific city (like Uzgand) may be specific but can become general if the city is large. Similarly, for cities like Samarkand and Bukhara, a neighborhood or alley is specific. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that mentioning the father suffices for identification, whereas 'the two' (possibly Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require mention of the grandfather, though fakhdh can substitute for grandfather. This shows the Hanafi school's attention to legal precision in procedural matters.

Key Terms
فخذ (fakhdh): The specific sub-tribe or clan that is directly above the family (fasila), such that there is no smaller named group.
طرفین (tarafayn): The two parties; in this context referring to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two besides Abu Yusuf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the function of mentioning the fakhdh according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) in the passage?
A) It replaces the father's name
B) It replaces the need to mention the grandfather
C) It makes the identification general
D) It is only required for women

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, there is a valid difference on whether the grandfather must be mentioned; using the fakhdh resolves the dispute and satisfies both views.
